PSKEYS.TXT
==========

Stack version:  10548 rck_16unified_fl_bt4.1_27d_1408131222_ble_encr128 2014-08-13

This file describes the firmware's pskeys.  (This single file replaces
the files user_keys.txt, developer_keys.txt and csr_keys.txt provided
with previous builds.)


==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_BDADDR (0x0001)

SUMMARY
	Bluetooth address

TYPE
	bdaddr

DEFAULT VALUE
	{ 0x00A5A5, 0x5b, 0x0002 }

DESCRIPTION
	The local device's Bluetooth address.  This should be unique to this
	device. It is allocated during manufacturing.
	
	The type bdaddr can be viewed as a uint16[4] array:
	
	        1st uint16:     The top 8 bits of the LAP are in the bottom 8
	                        bits of this word. The top 8 bits of this word
	                        must be zero.
	        2nd uint16:     The lower 16 bits of the LAP
	        3rd uint16:     The 8-bit UAP is in the bottom 8 bits of this
	                        word. The top 8 bits of this word must be
	                        zero.
	        4th uint16:     16-bit NAP
	
	For example, the Bluetooth address 123456789abc is encoded as 0078,
	9abc, 0056, 1234.
	
	The default value of this key is one of CSR's legal addresses:
	00025b00a5a5.
	
	As stated in the Bluetooth specification, LAP values from 9e8b00 up
	to, and including, 9e8b3f must not be used as this range is reserved
	for inquiry access codes (IACs).
	
	Bluetooth module manufacturers must obtain their own block of
	addresses from the Bluetooth SIG/IEEE. If CSR's experience is
	typical, these authorities define the NAP and UAP, allowing
	manufacturers to set the 24-bit LAP.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_CLASSOFDEVICE (0x0003)

SUMMARY
	Class of device

TYPE
	bdcod

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(0xffffff)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0)

DESCRIPTION
	The local device's default Bluetooth "Class of Device" or CoD.
	
	Type bdcod is really a uint32. The class of device is a 24-bit
	value stored in a uint32; the highest byte must be zero.
	
	This is the device's default class of device, used when the device
	boots. The device's class of device may subsequently be changed by
	an HCI command. The HCI command does not change the value stored
	under this PSKey.
	
	The least significant two bits reveal the format of the other 22
	bits. The only format currently defined is for where the two
	bits are zero:
	
	  Bits     Content
	  [1:0]    Format Type (0)
	  [7:2]    Minor Dev Class (in the context of the Major Dev Class)
	  [12:8]   Major Dev Class
	  [23:13]  Major Service Class
	
	At the time of writing, the firmware makes no use of this information.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_DEVICE_DRIFT (0x0004)

SUMMARY
	Device drift

TYPE
	uint16

MAXIMUM
	(250)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(250)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the local device's radio timing drift in parts per
	million. The maximum value allowed by the Bluetooth specification
	is 250.
	
	This value is used in LMP_timing_accuracy_res messages sent to
	peers, as described in Bluetooth version 1.1, LMP specification,
	section 5.2. It is also used in calculations in low power modes
	to decide for how long the radio on a slave device must be turned on
	in order to resynchronise with a remote master: reducing the value
	therefore allows power saving.
	
	The default value is appropriate when BlueCore's internal low power
	oscillator is in use to maintain timing during low power modes, i.e.  
	for the default setting of PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_STATE
	(DEEP_SLEEP_ALWAYS, value 1) and PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_USE_EXTERNAL_CLOCK
	(FALSE). The appropriate values for the various settings of these
	PSKeys are:
	
	PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_STATE = NEVER or INACTIVE (0 or 2): set device drift
	to 20 ppm to reflect full Bluetooth clock accuracy.
	
	PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_STATE = ALWAYS (1): if
	PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_USE_EXTERNAL_CLOCK is FALSE, set device drift to 250
	ppm (default). If an external clock is in use, set
	device drift to the accuracy of that external clock.
	
	PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_STATE = ALWAYS_ACCURATE (3):
	if PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_USE_EXTERNAL_CLOCK is TRUE, set device drift to
	the accuracy of the external slow clock.
	
	Note: Some BlueCore7 and later parts can internally derive a slow
	clock from their fast clock and so the accuracy will be much
	better than 250 ppm. See comments in PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_STATE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_DEVICE_JITTER (0x0005)

SUMMARY
	Device jitter

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(10)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the local device's radio jitter in microseconds.
	(LMP v1.1, section 5.2.)
	
	This value is used in LMP_timing_accuracy_res messages sent to
	peers.  This is the only use for this PSKey.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_MAX_ACLS (0x000d)

SUMMARY
	Maximum ACL links

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(40)

DEFAULT VALUE
	MAX_NUM_ACLS

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the maximum number of concurrent ACL connections to
	other devices.
	
	Links to remote devices use substantial amounts of RAM to maintain
	connection state, so this value should be kept low. It is
	advisable to trim this value to match the application, allowing any
	liberated RAM to be used elsewhere. The value must be reduced
	if the chip is running any of the higher layers of the Bluetooth
	stack because these take from the common supply of RAM.
	
	On 23h and later firmware, reducing this key can allow the malloc
	space freed up to be put into larger pools for VM applications. See
	the descriptions of PSKEY_PMALLOC_PER_ACL and PSKEY_PMALLOC_BASE for
	more information. (This key has no direct effect on malloc usage for
	earlier firmware.)

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_MAX_SCOS (0x000e)

SUMMARY
	Maximum SCO links

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(3)

DEFAULT VALUE
	MAX_NUM_SCOS

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the maximum number of SCO links to (all) other
	devices.
	
	On 23h and later firmware, reducing this key can allow the malloc
	space freed up to be put into larger pools for VM applications. See
	the descriptions of PSKEY_PMALLOC_PER_SCO and PSKEY_PMALLOC_BASE for
	more information. (This key has no direct effect on malloc usage for
	earlier firmware.)
	
	This value may be reduced to increase the buffer space available for
	ACL data: see the description of PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_ACL_PKT_LEN.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_MAX_REMOTE_MASTERS (0x000f)

SUMMARY
	Maximum remote masters

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(1)

MAXIMUM
	(2)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(2)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the local device's maximum number of remote piconet 
	masters.
	
	Connecting to multiple remote masters implies the use of scatternets.
	The current firmware supports one permanent remote master, plus a
	second remote master in a temporary state either for performing a
	remote name request or to connect by a role switch to become a slave.
	
	See the description of PSKEY_ENABLE_MASTERY_WITH_SLAVERY.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_ENABLE_MASTERY_WITH_SLAVERY (0x0010)

SUMMARY
	Support master and slave roles simultaneously

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(TRUE)

DESCRIPTION
	If this PSKey is set to TRUE (value 1) then the firmware is configured
	to support being a master of its own piconet at the same time as being
	a slave in one or more other piconets. This implies the use of
	scatternets.
	
	This value is constrained by the value of the PSKey
	PSKEY_MAX_REMOTE_MASTERS.
	
	The "barge-in" connection sequence (an existing master page-scans,
	it is paged by new a device, then the new device's link performs
	a master/slave switch) implies a temporary scatternet.  This PSKey
	does not effect this behaviour.
	
	See the description of PSKEY_MAX_REMOTE_MASTERS.
	
	(Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to
	FALSE and TRUE.)

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_ACL_PKT_LEN (0x0011)

SUMMARY
	Maximum HCI ACL packet length

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(1)

MAXIMUM
	(512)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(310)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the maximum acceptable length, in bytes, of the data 
	portion of HCI ACL data packets received from the host. This is
	reported by the HCI_Read_Buffer_Size HCI command as the
	HC_ACL_Data_Packet_Length value.
	
	You may want to tune this value to obtain better device throughput.
	However, you must keep constant the product of the values of this key
	and of total number of host packets. Because this effectively
	reserves a block of the device's valuable RAM for use by the host.
	
	For each SCO connection 1024 bytes of memory is reserved and if the
	max number of SCO connections (N)= PSKEY_MAX_SCOS is reduced by 1
	from its firmware default, the effective total memory for ACL and
	fastpipe packets may be increased by 1024 bytes.
	
	On parts that do not support ram reserve feature total number of
	host packets is taken from PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_ACL_PKTS. On these
	parts, if B = PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_ACL_PKTS,
	L = PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_ACL_PKT_LEN, and S is product B * L, when
	these keys have their firmware default values then the following
	four conditions must be satisfied if these keys are altered:
	
	If the parts support EDR:
	1. B * L <= S
	2. B * L <= 3968
	3. (B + 1) * L <= 4095
	4. B <= 14
	
	If the parts do not support EDR:
	1. B * L <= S
	2. B * L <= 1919
	3. (B + 1) * L <= 2047
	4. B <= 14
	
	On parts that support ram reserve feature, total memory reserved for
	host (PSKEY_MMU_TRACKED_BYTES) is sum of buffers for ACL packets,
	buffers for fastpipe packets and SCO buffers. On these following are
	the parameters used to determine the max number of ACL packets.
	-> T = Tokens set by allocate_ram_reserve BCCMD
	-> B = HC_Total_Num_ACL_Data_Packets returned by HCI_Read_Buffer_Size
	       HCI command (which includes T) + PSKEY_RESERVE_INIT_TOKENS
	-> L = PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_ACL_PKT_LEN
	-> N = PSKEY_MAX_SCOS
	
	With above parameters following conditions must be satisfied if these
	keys are altered:
	
	1. (B * L) + (N * 1024) <= PSKEY_MMU_TRACKED_BYTES (6236)
	2. B * L <= 4032
	3. (B + 1) * L <= 4095
	4. B <= 14
	
	Violating any of these conditions may cause the chip to crash or
	behave oddly. CSR only supports configurations that meet all four
	of these conditions.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_SCO_PKT_LEN (0x0012)

SUMMARY
	Maximum HCI SCO packet length

TYPE
	uint8

MINIMUM
	(1)

MAXIMUM
	(128)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(64)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the maximum acceptable length, in bytes, of the data 
	portion of HCI SCO data packets received from the host. This supports
	the HCI_Read_Buffer_Size HCI command.
	
	You may want to tune this value to obtain better device
	throughput. However, you must keep constant the product of the values
	of this key and of PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_SCO_PKTS because this effectively
	reserves a block of the device's valuable RAM for use by the host.
	
	Only change this value after careful consideration: small values
	will heavily load the (host and) chip processor(s), and large
	values will normally increase audio latency.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_SCO_PKTS (0x0014)

SUMMARY
	Maximum number of HCI SCO packets

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(1)

MAXIMUM
	(14)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(8)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the maximum number of HCI SCO data packets being sent
	to air that can be held within the chip at any time.
	
	This supports the HCI_Read_Buffer_Size HCI command.
	
	See the description of PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_SCO_PKT_LEN.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LC_FC_BUFFER_LOW_WATER_MARK (0x0015)

SUMMARY
	Flow control low water mark

TYPE
	lc_fc_lwm

DEFAULT VALUE
	{0x0600, 0x0700, 0x0800}

DESCRIPTION
	This PS Key holds a set of values that control the assertion of flow 
	control for data received from air.
	
	The LC determines how much buffer memory has been promised to
	the host for host to air traffic, then it adds the safety margins
	set by this key and compares the result with the available free
	buffer memory. The result determines when and how the LC applies
	flow control for data received from air.
	
	This PSKey holds an array of three values. Each value sets a behaviour
	threshold, measured in a number of bytes:
	
	        0: Received data is discarded and a NAK is returned
	        1: ACL flow control is asserted
	        2: L2CAP flow control is asserted
	

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LC_MAX_TX_POWER (0x0017)

SUMMARY
	Maximum transmit power

TYPE
	int16

MINIMUM
	(-128)

MAXIMUM
	(127)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(20)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the device's maximum transmit power in dBm.
	
	The firmware ensures the device never speaks more loudly than this
	value.
	
	The firmware uses the highest value in the power table that is less
	than or equal to the requested default power.
	
	Correct operation depends on having a valid power table - see
	PSKEY_LC_POWER_TABLE.
	
	The maximum value depends on the Bluetooth module class:
	
	        Class 1:  0  to +20 dBm.
	        Class 2:  -6 to +4  dBm.
	        Class 3:  up to 0   dBm.
	
	Unlike most PSKey values, this is a *signed* 16-bit integer.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_TX_GAIN_RAMP (0x001d)

SUMMARY
	Transmit gain ramp rate

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(4)

MAXIMUM
	(0xffff)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x1810)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the device's transmitter gain ramp rate. It controls 
	the power ramp-up at the start of a packet and ramp-down at the end of
	a packet.
	
	CSR recommends that this value is not modified from the default.
	
	Bits [7:0] control the ramp rate. The normal range is between 0x04
	and 0x3F. Values below 0x04 are out of spec and must not be used.
	
	Bits [15:8] control the length of the unmodulated carrier between the 
	end of the ramp and the start of the packet in microseconds.
	
	The ramp rate value has different effects according to whether the 
	module uses the chip's internal power amplifier or an external 
	amplifier. (See PSKEY_TXRX_PIO_CONTROL.)
	
	If the internal power amplifier is ramped then the microseconds taken
	to complete the ramp is 
	   (4*amplifier_setting)/ramp_rate.
	
	If an external power amplifier is ramped then the microseconds taken
	to complete the ramp is 
	   (amplifier_setting)/ramp_rate
	
	In both cases amplifier_setting is taken from the power table 
	PSKEY_LC_ENHANCED_POWER_TABLE (PSKEY_LC_POWER_TABLE on older BlueCore
	devices where EDR is not supported).
	
	The total time controlled by this PS key is
	    ramp_time (calculated as above) + unmodulated_carrier_time

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LC_FC_POOLS_LOW_WATER_MARK (0x0020)

SUMMARY
	Flow control pool low water mark

TYPE
	lc_fc_lwm

DEFAULT VALUE
	{0x0014, 0x0018, 0x001a}

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey is similar to PSKEY_LC_FC_BUFFER_LOW_WATER_MARK, but
	describes numbers of available pool memory blocks.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LC_DEFAULT_TX_POWER (0x0021)

SUMMARY
	Default transmit power

TYPE
	int16

MINIMUM
	(-128)

MAXIMUM
	(127)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(4)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the radio's default transmit power, measured in dBm. 
	The chip uses this for page, inquiry and their scan responses. This is
	also the power used for new connections.
	
	In 12.X builds the firmware uses the entry in the power table that is
	closest to this PSKey's value. If the two closest power tables are
	equidistant from this key's value then it is indeterminate which
	power table entry is used.
	
	In 13.X and later builds the firmware uses the highest value in the
	power table that is less than or equal to the requested default
	power.
	
	Correct operation depends on the the device having a valid power
	table - see PSKEY_LC_POWER_TABLE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LC_MAX_TX_POWER_NO_RSSI (0x002d)

SUMMARY
	Maximum transmit power when peer has no RSSI

TYPE
	int8

DEFAULT VALUE
	(4)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey value is used after a connection is made, if it is found
	that a remote device does not support RSSI measurements or the local
	device does not support power control. The transmit power is lowered
	to correspond to the first entry in PSKEY_LC_POWER_TABLE whose power
	in dBm is less than or equal to the value of this PSKey.
	
	According to the Bluetooth specification, a device may only
	transmit to a receiving device that does not support the necessary
	messaging for sending the power control messages
	using the rules for a class 2 or class 3 device, in other
	words, with a maximum transmit power of 4 dBm, hence the default value
	for this PSKey. This allows the default transmit power to be raised
	above 4 dBm without violating the specification.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LC_CONNECTION_RX_WINDOW (0x002e)

SUMMARY
	Receive window size during connections

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(10)

DESCRIPTION
	The Bluetooth specification requires that a master or slave is
	sensitive to timing jitter of transmissions from the other side up to
	10 microseconds while the two devices are connected. The value may be
	controlled by this PSKey.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_BT_CLOCK_INIT (0x0034)

SUMMARY
	Initial value of Bluetooth clock

TYPE
	uint32

MAXIMUM
	(0xfffffffUL)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0UL)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the value to which the Bluetooth clock is initialised
	at boot. The value 0 is standard; the only likely reason to alter this
	is for debugging non-CSR devices known to encounter problems at
	certain clock values.
	
	Historical note:  before this key was introduced, CSR devices
	initialised their Bluetooth clocks from the lower 28 bits of the
	Bluetooth address, i.e. the lower 4 bits of the UAP followed by
	the LAP.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_CONDITIONAL_SCAN_ENABLE (0x0036)

SUMMARY
	Enable conditional scan

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(FALSE)

DESCRIPTION
	If this PSKey is set to TRUE (value 1), the firmware rapidly scans the
	Bluetooth band on the first slot pair of a page or inquiry scan,
	looking for any transmissions in the band. If it finds none, it does
	not listen for the remaining scan window. The intention is to save
	power when there are no other devices nearby.

==============================================================================

	PSKEY_TX_MR_MOD_DELAY (0x0038)

SUMMARY
	TX Mod delay

TYPE
	uint8

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x59)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds mod delay for Tx.

NAME
	PSKEY_RX_MR_SYNC_CONFIG (0x003a)

SUMMARY
	RX MR Sync Configuration

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x0024)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds acceptable correlation quality of EDR.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LC_LOST_SYNC_SLOTS (0x003b)

SUMMARY
	Time in ms for lost sync in low power modes

TYPE
	uint16

MAXIMUM
	(0x7fff)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0)

DESCRIPTION
	In low power modes, a device considers it has lost synchronisation
	with its peer if it fails to receive an expected transmission in one
	of the following circumstances:
	
	- In sniff mode as a slave, during any sniff window when nothing
	is received.
	
	- In sniff mode as a master, during any sniff window when the slave
	has been sent a POLL or a data packet and no reply has been
	received.
	
	- In park mode as a slave, when no transmission is received on any
	park beacon in a train.
	
	This PSKey specifies a value in baseband slots (units of 625 us) which
	must elapse since the last packet received from the remote device
	before the logic described above applies.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_RX_MR_SAMP_CONFIG (0x003c)

SUMMARY
	RX MR Sync Configuration

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x0426)

DESCRIPTION
	Acceptable correlation quality of EDR

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_NO_CAL_ON_BOOT (0x0042)

SUMMARY
	Do not calibrate radio on boot

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(FALSE)

DESCRIPTION
	Set this PSKey to TRUE to cause the LC not to calibrate the radio at
	boot time. This means that the radio does not work until the key is
	set to false and the chip is rebooted. This key is intended to allow
	the use of a bootmode where the radio is disabled. For details on
	bootmodes, see the CSR document "Understanding and Using Bootmodes",
	CS-101528-AN (previously numbered as bcore-an-019P),
	on the CSR support website.
	
	Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to
	FALSE and TRUE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_RSSI_HI_TARGET (0x0043)

SUMMARY
	RSSI high target

TYPE
	uint8

DEFAULT VALUE
	(80)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey controls a parameter used by BlueCore's automatic gain
	control (AGC) algorithm. Do not change it except on specific advice
	from CSR.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LC_ENABLE_LATE_SAMPLE (0x004b)

SUMMARY
	Enable late data sampling for transmission

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(TRUE)

ENUM_INCLUDE_FILE
	bt.h

ENUM_VALUES
	 TRUE (1)   Enabled
	FALSE (0)   Disabled

DESCRIPTION
	This key controls when the LC should sample if data is available
	for transmission.  If enabled the LC samples as late as possible
	for data being available.

	PSKEY_LC_CLOCKS_CONFIG (0x004f)

SUMMARY
	Miscellaneous Bluetooth hardware clock config

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey enables miscellaneous configuration of hardware clocks for 
	Bluetooth.
	
	Do not change this PSKey except on specific advice from CSR.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_EDR_SWITCH_MODE (0x0051)

SUMMARY
	EDR power amp, assertion method  

TYPE
	edr_switch_mode

DEFAULT VALUE
	(HIGH_TO_LOW)

ENUM_INCLUDE_FILE
	io_bt.h

ENUM_VALUES
	HIGH_TO_LOW   high to low transition on pio pin
	LOW_TO_HIGH   low to high transition on pio pin

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the EDR_SWITCH_MODE which is used to describe the 
	assertion method for the EDR_SWITCH_MODE_PIO and is used to set up
	the driving method, Low To High or High To Low.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_EDR_MODE_SWITCH_PIO (0x0052)

SUMMARY
	EDR PA support on pio(x) 

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	<none>

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey asserts the PIO line specified, 0-15 if present. If 
	the PSKey is not present it becomes a zero-length key with 
	an attempt to read it failing. This fails the psget method 
	and disables use of this key. If the PSKey is defined but the value 
	is 0xffff, out of bounds, then the key does not set up a PIO line. 
	Using this PSKey is intended to be the mode select line for 
	an EDR power amp. The assertion method is in 
	PSKEY EDR_SWITCH_MODE and will be either high to low or low to 
	high.
	
	If a PIO line is required for Tx enabling then you should use 
	PSKEY_TXRX_PIO_CONTROL, pio pin 1 which asserts when transmitting.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LC_ENABLE_WATCHDOG_FAULT (0x0053)

SUMMARY
	Enable LC watchdog fault reporting

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(FALSE)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey is a debugging option for CSR internal use only.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LC_PEER_POWER_INCR_PERIOD (0x0057)

SUMMARY
	Peer transmit power control interval

TYPE
	TIME

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(60 * SECOND)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(100000)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey is the period, measured in microseconds, between attempts
	to increment the peer's transmit power. 
	
	Set this PSKey to zero to disable the periodic checks. This means the
	local device does not send messages concerning power management or 
	channel quality driven data rate to the remote device. This PSKey
	is paired with decrement peer power period.
	
	Type TIME is fundamentally a uint32.  Value SECOND is 1000000.
	Value MILLISECOND is 1000.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LC_PEER_POWER_DECR_PERIOD (0x0058)

SUMMARY
	Peer transmit power control interval

TYPE
	TIME

MINIMUM
	(100000)

MAXIMUM
	(60 * SECOND)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(1 * SECOND)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey is the period, measured in microseconds, between attempts
	to decrement the peer's transmit power. The same interval is used for 
	measurements of channel quality to support LMP channel quality driven
	data rate messages.
	
	This PSKey is paired with the respective increment peer power period.
	This key has a minimum value of 100 ms. However it is disabled if the 
	increment peer power period is set to 0. This means the local device
	does not send messages concerning peer power management.
	
	Type TIME is fundamentally a uint32.  Value SECOND is 1000000.
	Value MILLISECOND is 1000.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LC_HIGH_PRIORITY_SNIFF_TIMEOUTS (0x0060)

SUMMARY
	High priority bandwidth for sniff timeout slots

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(FALSE)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey affects the algorithm that selects the value of Dsniff when
	negotiating sniff mode for an ACL connection.  If no value is set or
	the value is FALSE, sniff timeout slots are not included in the
	calculation unless the quality of service for the connection is
	"guaranteed". If the value is TRUE, sniff timeout slots are always
	taken into account: this means that extra spacing is left in the
	air time schedule, where possible, to allow for a transmission to a
	slave during one iteration of the timeout slots.
	
	This PSKey has no direct effect on the real-time scheduling of links
	in sniff mode, so it does not necessarily cause a master to address
	the slave in the timeout slots. A QoS setting of "guaranteed" for an
	ACL connection causes sniff timeout slots to be treated as high
	priority by the real-time scheduler. However, use this with caution
	because it can have a significant effect on the bandwidth available
	for other links.
	
	Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to
	FALSE and TRUE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_USB_BCD_DEVICE (0x007d)

SUMMARY
	USB device release number in BCD

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	<none>

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the bcdDevice field of the local USB device, as
	defined in Table 9.8 of version 2.0 of the USB specification. This is
	held in BCD.
	
	If this PSKey is not set, the firmware reports its own build
	identifier number.
	
	The value is only used if the chip is presenting its USB interface,
	and for the DFU_GETDEVICE request when using DFU over UART.
	
	See the description of PSKEY_HOST_INTERFACE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LINK_KEY_BD_ADDR0 (0x00ca)

SUMMARY
	Bluetooth address + link key 0

TYPE
	LM_LINK_KEY_BD_ADDR_T

DEFAULT VALUE
	<none>

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets a Bluetooth address and its corresponding link key:
	        1st uint16:     top 8 bits of the LAP in the lower byte
	        2nd uint16:     lower 16 bits of the LAP
	        3rd uint16:     16-bit UAP
	        4th uint16:     8-bit NAP in the lower byte
	Link key is 8 words, following the 4-word BDADDR. The link key
	is stored little-endian, so MSW is at position 11, LSW at
	position 4.
	Occupied keys should appear in PSKEY_FREE_KEY_PIGEON_HOLE.

	bits, etc.

	Section 14.3.3, p161, 3rd paragraph: maximum key size between one and

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LOCAL_SUPPORTED_FEATURES (0x00ef)

SUMMARY
	Local supported features block

TYPE
	uint16[4]

DEFAULT VALUE
	{ 0xffff, 0xfe8f, 0xffdb, 0x875b }

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds a 4-element array of uint16s holding a bitfield that 
	describes the features supported by the local device for page 0 of the
	device features bits mentioned in the LMP specification.
	
	See PSKEY_LOCAL_SUPPORTED_FEATURES_PAGE_2 for the page 2 features.
	Note that PSKEY_LOCAL_SUPPORTED_FEATURES_PAGE_2 is only present
	in BlueCore firmware images which support page 2 features.
	
	Coding matches the "coding of features" section in the LMP
	specification. The first byte of the coding of features is held in
	the lower byte of the first uint16, etc.
	
	The key's default value gives the firmware's capabilities. Switching
	a bit from 0 to 1 does not create a missing capability.
	
	This PSKey configures the local LM. If a feature is marked as provided
	by the default value, then clearing the key's bit turns off the
	corresponding functionality. For example, setting the Encryption bit
	to zero stops the local device supporting encryption.
	
	The three "flow control lag" bits should be left at zero.
	
	The order in 1.2 of the specification is:
	
	First word, low to high (X => turned on in default config;
	(X) => turned on if supported by hardware;)
	  On   Bit   Feature
	   X   0     3-slot packets
	   X   1     5-slot packets
	   X   2     Encryption
	   X   3     Slot offset
	   X   4     Timing accuracy
	   X   5     Master/slave switch
	   X   6     Hold mode
	   X   7     Sniff mode
	   X   8     Park mode
	   X   9     Power control requests
	   X  10     Data rate driven by channel quality
	   X  11     SCO link
	   X  12     HV2 packets
	   X  13     HV3 packets
	   X  14     mu-law voice encoding
	   X  15     A-law voice encoding
	
	Second word
	   X   0     CVSD
	   X   1     Paging scheme
	   X   2     Power control
	   X   3     Transparent SCO data
	       4     }
	       5     } L2CAP flow control lag (our default = 0)
	       6     }
	          [1.2 features from this point]
	   X   7     Broadcast encryption
	       8     Reserved (Scatter mode)
	  (X)  9     Enhanced Data Rate ACL 2 Mbps mode
	  (X) 10     Enhanced Data Rate ACL 3 Mbps mode
	   X  11     Enhanced inquiry scan
	   X  12     Interlaced inquiry scan
	   X  13     Interlaced page scan
	   X  14     RSSI with inquiry results
	  (X) 15     Extended SCO link --- EV3 packets
	
	Third word
	  (X)  0     Extended SCO link --- EV4 packets
	  (X)  1     Extended SCO link --- EV5 packets
	       2     Reserved (Absence masks)
	   X   3     AFH capable slave
	   X   4     AFH classification slave
	       5     BR/EDR not supported
	       6     LE supported (Controller)
	  (X)  7     3-slot Enhanced Data Rate ACL packets
	  (X)  8     5-slot Enhanced Data Rate ACL packets
	   X   9     Sniff Subrating
	   X  10     Pause Encryption
	   X  11     AFH capable master
	   X  12     AFH classification master
	  (X) 13     Enhanced Data Rate eSCO 2 Mbps mode
	  (X) 14     Enhanced Data Rate eSCO 3 Mbps mode
	  (X) 15     3-slot Enhanced Data Rate eSCO packets
	
	Fourth word
	   X   0     Extended Inquiry Response
	       1     Simultaneous LE and BR/EDR to same device capable
	             (Controller)
	       2     Reserved
	   X   3     Secure Simple Pairing
	   X   4     Encapsulated PDU
	       5     Erroneous Data Reporting
	   X   6     Non-flushable Packet Boundary Flag
	       7     Reserved
	   X   8     Link Supervision Timeout Changed Event
	   X   9     Inquiry Response TX Power Level
	   X  10     Enhanced Power Control
	      11-14  Reserved     
	   X  15     Extended features [i.e. highest bit in feature mask]

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HCI_NOP_DISABLE (0x00f2)

SUMMARY
	Disable the HCI Command_Status event on boot

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(FALSE)

DESCRIPTION
	By default the BlueCore firmware sends an HCI command_status(NOP)
	event to the host shortly after booting. Although this is clearly
	allowed by the HCI specification it is known to crash some host
	stacks.
	
	This PSKey provides a simple workaround: if this key is TRUE then
	this boot-time event is not emitted.
	
	Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to
	FALSE and TRUE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LM_MAX_EVENT_FILTERS (0x00f4)

SUMMARY
	Maximum number of event filters

TYPE
	uint8

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(255)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(5)

DESCRIPTION
	Each time an event filter is added, it consumes valuable RAM
	resources. To limit the maximum amount of RAM event filters can
	take this PSKey limits the maximum number of event filters.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LM_TEST_SEND_ACCEPTED_TWICE (0x00f6)

SUMMARY
	LM sends two LMP_accepted messages in test mode

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(FALSE)

DESCRIPTION
	The Bluetooth v1.1 specification does not ensure reliability of LMP
	traffic in test mode, because it does not differentiate test packets
	(which are unreliable) from LMP packets at the baseband level. This
	can lead to loss of LMP messages.
	
	If this PSKey is set to TRUE, a slave in test mode sends the
	LMP_Accepted reply to a test control message twice. This increases
	the likelihood that the message will be received by the tester. (It
	does not guarantee it because, as the link manager does not operate
	in real time, there may be test messages in between the
	transmissions.)
	
	Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to
	FALSE and TRUE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LM_MAX_PAGE_HOLD_TIME (0x00f7)

SUMMARY
	Maximum time we hold a device around page

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(65535)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0)

DESCRIPTION
	Each time a unit pages a new device and it currently has active links,
	they are held for page timeout slots. If page timeout slots is greater
	than this PSKey value, this value is used a the maximum hold time.
	A value of zero indicates that holding around page is disabled.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_AFH_ADAPTATION_RESPONSE_TIME (0x00f8)

SUMMARY
	LM period for AFH adaption

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(0x0640)

MAXIMUM
	(0xBB80)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x12c0)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the interval between successive channel classification
	updates (and hence channel map adaptations) for an AFH enabled master.
	The period is measured in baseband slots (625us), and is between 1 and
	30 seconds.
	
	The slave classification intervals sent in the
	LMP_channel_classfication_req message are derived from this value:
	    AFH_max_interval = this_value
	    AFH_min_interval = this_value / 2

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_AFH_OPTIONS (0x00f9)

SUMMARY
	Options to configure AFH

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x0017)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey allows you to configure AFH. The bits are not restricted to
	classification, as follows:
	 Bit 0 enable RSSI classification
	 Bit 1 enable PLR classification
	 Bit 2 enable use of combo information in classification
	 Bit 3 <reserved>
	 Bit 4 enable hysterisis of the classifications from slaves
	 Bit 5 disable RSSI classification with "low power" links
	 Bit 6 enable extended RSSI classification with "low power" links,
	       this enables the time period for RSSI classification to be
	       PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_LP_RUN_PERIOD.
	
	RSSI - BlueCore makes signal strength measurements of channels not
	being used by the Bluetooth link when the radio would otherwise be
	idle. In ideal radio conditions, this increases the power 
	consumption during a connection. However, it has the advantage that 
	it makes Bluetooth a good neighbour; it identifies and avoids other 
	users of the ISM band even if they are not causing problems for 
	Bluetooth operation and can return channels to use when the 
	interferer is no longer present. Power consumption can be reduced 
	with interference present as there is a reduced need for 
	message retransmissions. CSR recommends that RSSI is enabled.
	
	When all links are "low power", power consumption for RSSI
	classification can be reduced by not performing RSSI scans (setting
	Bit 5), or performing them less regularly (setting Bit 6 and setting
	PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_LP_RUN_PERIOD larger than PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_RUN_PERIOD).
	"Low power" links are in sniff or park with a period of more than 128
	slots. (This value was chosen to distinguish sniff periods used in HID
	devices from those used by, for example, idle headsets.)
	
	Note: A link is never considered to be "low power" if it has a SCO
	or eSCO link associated with it, so that adding an (e)SCO link to a
	sniffed link immediately restarts or speeds up classification when
	using Bits 5 or 6 of this PSKey.
	
	PLR - Dropped packets and bit error rates for FEC encoded headers and
	payloads are used to estimate the interference for each of the
	channels being used. This gives priority to channels that are
	degrading the Bluetooth performance. As mentioned above, it does not
	identify other users of the ISM band unless they are corrupting
	Bluetooth packets, and it does not rapidly detect the removal of an
	interferer on a channel being avoided. Additionally, BlueCore can 
	only apply this method when it is master of the link.
	
	To use AFH functionality to avoid interference, at least one device in
	the link must include a classifier.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_RUN_PERIOD (0x00fa)

SUMMARY
	AFH RSSI reading period

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(50)

MAXIMUM
	(0xFFFF)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(500)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the period with which the LC schedules an RSSI
	classification. When this period has passed, and there is a gap in
	Bluetooth activity, the Bluetooth radio is used as a spectrum analyser
	to read the RSSI on all Bluetooth channels. These values are averaged
	and decay slowly.
	
	Note: Bit 6 of PSKEY_AFH_OPTIONS allows a longer period to be used
	for links in sniff and park. See the descriptions of PSKEY_AFH_OPTIONS
	and PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_LP_RUN_PERIOD for more information.
	
	The value of this PSKey is in units of ms.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_AFH_REENABLE_CHANNEL_TIME (0x00fb)

SUMMARY
	AFH good channel adding time

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(0x00FA)

MAXIMUM
	(0xFFFF)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x0FA0)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey determines the amount of time it takes for a channel that
	was marked as bad to be marked as good again (when there is no further
	information about that channel). The time is approximately Key *
	40 milliseconds. The actual time varies, as reintroduction is
	deliberately randomised. The fastest possible time is 25% of this
	time.
	
	In the presence of broadband signals, the time to mark the channels 
	affected by these signals is increased. This reduces the 
	chance of further interference from the broadband source - which may 
	be caused by beacons or varying data transfer on the broadband signal.
	
	Channels are typically marked as unknown much sooner than this.  
	AFH selection algorithms may use this as a hint to use the 
	channel sooner.
	
	The value of this PSKey is in units of 40 ms.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_NO_DROP_ON_ACR_MS_FAIL (0x00fc)

SUMMARY
	Complete link if acr barge-in role switch refused

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(TRUE)

DESCRIPTION
	If the Role parameter to the HCI Accept_Connection_Request (acr)
	command is 0x00 it requires the local device to become master of the
	link. This means requesting the existing (paging) master to
	perform a role switch, and only completing the connection if the
	switch is performed. The link is dropped if the request to perform a
	role switch is refused. You can configure the HCI Set_Event_Filter 
	command to achieve the same behaviour without involving the host
	via Connection_Request.
	
	Set the PSKey to TRUE to alter this behaviour: if the Role
	parameter is 0x00 then it is treated as advice - the local device
	requests the paging master to perform a role switch, but the link is
	not dropped if this is refused. The behaviour of the event filter is
	similarly adjusted. No attempt is made to hide a failure to switch.
	For example, no Role_Change event is sent to the host.
	
	This PSKey attempts to fix situations where both devices insist on 
	being master. However, it changes the behaviour of HCI, so there is no
	guarantee that a given host stack will behave correctly. You must 
	determine the correct system operation.
	
	If this PSKey is FALSE, the firmware provides the normal HCI
	behaviour.
	
	Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to
	FALSE and TRUE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LOCAL_SUPPORTED_COMMANDS (0x0106)

SUMMARY
	Local supported commands

TYPE
	uint16[9..32]

DEFAULT VALUE
	{0xffff, 0x03ff, 0xfffe, 0xffff, 
                         0xffff, 0xffff, 0x0ff3, 0xfee8, 
                         0xf73f, 0xff83, 0x001C, 0x0000, 
                         0xf761, 0xffff, 0x007f, 0x0000, 
                         0x0000}

DESCRIPTION
	
	This PSKey holds a large bitfield (in little-endian format) that 
	describes which HCI commands are supported by the host controller. 
	The Host finds out this information by trying the command. The Host
	Controller then returns with "Unknown HCI Command", but some
	Hosts might prefer to try this command first.
	
	The result returned by this command does not change after the Host
	Controller has booted. Sometimes it is not possible for the Host
	Controller to perform some operations (eg. insufficient resources or
	not having a link of the correct type).  This command still implies
	that the commands are available; if the Host tries such a command the
	Host Controller should return a different status message than "Unknown
	HCI Command".
	
	Byte 0:
	        0 Inquiry
	        1 Inquiry Cancel
	        2 Periodic Inquiry Mode
	        3 Exit Periodic Inquiry Mode
	        4 Create Connection
	        5 Disconnect
	        6 Add SCO Connection
	        7 Cancel Create Connection
	
	Byte 1:
	        0 Accept Connection Request
	        1 Reject Connection Request
	        2 Link Key Request Reply
	        3 Link Key Request Negative Reply
	        4 PIN Code Request Reply
	        5 PIN Code Request Negative Reply
	        6 Change Connection Packet Type
	        7 Authentication Request
	
	Byte 2:
	        0 Set Connection Encryption
	        1 Change Connection Link Key
	        2 Master Link Key
	        3 Remote Name Request
	        4 Cancel Remote Name Request
	        5 Read Remote Supported Features
	        6 Read Remote Extended Features
	        7 Read Remote Version Information
	
	Byte 3:
	        0 Read Clock Offset
	        1 Read LMP Handle
	        2 <reserved> Exchange Fixed Info
	        3 <reserved> Exchange Alias Info
	        4 <reserved> Private Pairing Request Reply
	        5 <reserved> Private Pairing Request Negative Reply
	        6 <reserved> Generated Alias
	        7 <reserved> Alias Address Request Reply
	
	Byte 4:
	        0 <reserved> Alias Address Request Negative Reply
	        1 Hold Mode
	        2 Sniff Mode
	        3 Exit Sniff Mode
	        4 Park Mode
	        5 Exit Park Mode
	        6 QoS Setup
	        7 Role Discovery
	
	Byte 5:
	        0 Switch Role
	        1 Read Link Policy Settings
	        2 Write Link Policy Settings
	        3 Read Default Link Policy Settings
	        4 Write Default Link Policy Settings
	        5 Flow Specification
	        6 Set Event Mark
	        7 Reset
	
	Byte 6:
	        0 Set Event Filter
	        1 Flush
	        2 Read PIN Type
	        3 Write PIN Type
	        4 Create New Unit Key
	        5 Read Stored Link Key
	        6 Write Stored Link Key
	        7 Delete Stored Link Key
	
	Byte 7:
	        0 Write Local Name
	        1 Read Local Name
	        2 Read Connection Accept Timeout
	        3 Write Connection Accept Timeout
	        4 Read Page Timeout
	        5 Write Page Timeout
	        6 Read Scan Enable
	        7 Write Scan Enable
	
	Byte 8:
	        0 Read Page Scan Activity
	        1 Write Page Scan Activity
	        2 Read Inquiry Scan Activity
	        3 Write Inquiry Scan Activity
	        4 Read Authentication Enable
	        5 Write Authentication Enable
	        6 Read Encryption Mode
	        7 Write Encryption Mode
	
	Byte 9:
	        0 Read Class Of Device
	        1 Write Class Of Device
	        2 Read Voice Setting
	        3 Write Voice Setting
	        4 Read Automatic Flush Timeout
	        5 Write Automatic Flush Timeout
	        6 Read Num Broadcast Retransmissions
	        7 Write Num Broadcast Retransmissions
	
	Byte 10:
	        0 Read Hold Mode Activity
	        1 Write Hold Mode Activity
	        2 Read Transmit Power Level
	        3 Read SCO Flow Control Enable
	        4 Write SCO Flow Control Enable
	        5 Set Host Controller To Host Flow Control
	        6 Host Buffer Size
	        7 Host Number Of Completed Packets
	
	Byte 11:
	        0 Read Link Supervision Timeout
	        1 Write Link Supervision Timeout
	        2 Read Number of Supported IAC
	        3 Read Current IAC LAP
	        4 Write Current IAC LAP
	        5 Read Page Scan Period Mode
	        6 Write Page Scan Period Mode
	        7 Read Page Scan Mode
	
	Byte 12:
	        0 Write Page Scan Mode
	        1 Set AFH Channel Classification
	        2 <reserved> (Read Extended Data Mode)
	        3 <reserved> (Write Extended Data Mode)
	        4 Read Inquiry Scan Type
	        5 Write Inquiry Scan Type
	        6 Read Inquiry Mode
	        7 Write Inquiry Mode
	
	Byte 13:
	        0 Read Page Scan Type
	        1 Write Page Scan Type
	        2 Read Channel Classification Mode
	        3 Write Channel Classification Mode

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_DEVICE_NAME (0x0108)

SUMMARY
	Local device's "user friendly" name

TYPE
	uint16[]

MAXIMUM
	(40)

DEFAULT VALUE
	{0x5343, 0x2052, 0x202d, 0x6362, 0x0037}

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the local device's default "user friendly" name, 
	used by the HCI Read_Local_Name and Change_Local_Name commands and by
	LMP_name_req/LMP_name_res transactions.
	
	When the firmware is booted, the device's name is taken from this
	PSKey. However, if the local host alters the local device's name, by
	calling the HCI Change_Local_Name command, then the new name is held
	in RAM. Subsequent requests to read the device's name take from the
	RAM store, not from this PSKey. The PSKey's value only becomes
	visible again after the firmware reboots.
	
	The Bluetooth v1.1 HCI specification requires the device's default
	name to be ""; an empty string. The default (psrom) value of this
	PSKey is "CSR - bc3" or similar. Therefore, the psrom value does not
	meet the HCI specification. If this PSKey is set to hold nothing,
	i.e., no uint16s are stored under the PSKey, then the HCI default
	value is obtained.
	
	Over HCI and LMP the name is passed as a sequence of UTF-8 octets.
	Because the PS stores data in arrays of uint16s, the name is packed
	in this PSKey, two octets per uint16. This packing is important when
	the PS store is small, notably where the PS is held in EEPROM.
	
	Working from the start of the device's name, the first character is
	stored in the lower octet of the PSKey's first uint16, the second
	character in the upper octet of the first uint16, etc. If the name
	is an odd number of characters then the upper octet of the last
	uint16 is '\0'.
	
	This PSKey can hold a maximum of 20 uint16s, limiting the default
	device name to 40 octets. The behaviour is undefined in this PSKey
	holds more than 20 uint16s. (This size constraint does not apply to
	a name written via the HCI Change_Local_Name command.)
	
	The default name for BlueCore3 chips is "CSR - bc3"; when packed this
	becomes {0x5343, 0x2052, 0x202d, 0x6362, 0x0033}.
	
	This PSKey is used from (HCI) 18.X builds.  HCI 17.X and earlier
	builds use PSKEY_LOCAL_NAME0 -> PSKEY_LOCAL_NAME17 and
	PSKEY_LOCAL_NAME_LENGTH.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_THRESHOLD (0x0109)

SUMMARY
	AFH RSSI threshold

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x0400)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds a value that controls the threshold of the entire 
	RSSI classification algorithm. If the standard deviation of the power 
	in the band is below this level then the device assumes that the
	entire band is clear and adapts its channel ratings accordingly.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_LM_CASUAL_SCAN_INTERVAL (0x010a)

SUMMARY
	Scan interval in slots for casual scanning

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	<none>

DESCRIPTION
	If this PSKey is set and is non-zero, `casual scanning' is enabled.
	The value then gives a maximum interval in slots between page and
	inquiry scans.
	
	In this mode, page and inquiry scans are not necessarily performed
	with the frequency of the intervals set via
	HCI_write_inquiry_scan_activity and HCI_write_page_scan_activity.  If
	the chip is active at any point after the interval specified over HCI
	since the previous scan, it performs the scan of the appropriate
	type. If it does not become active within
	PSKEY_LM_CASUAL_SCAN_INTERVAL slots after the previous scan, it 
	performs the scan at that point.
	
	On chips prior to BlueCore3-ROM, casual wakeup relies on the chip
	being woken up for some other reason, either by the host or due to an
	internal timer.
	
	Casual wakeup is most useful on hardware starting with BlueCore3-ROM.
	This contains support for waking the chip from deep sleep if the host
	provides a clock. In this case, if the host provides a clock at any
	time after the normal scan interval, the chip wakes to perform the
	scan in synchronisation with the host. Otherwise, it waits until
	PSKEY_LM_CASUAL_SCAN_INTERVAL slots have elapsed and wake anyway.
	
	For this reason you should only set this PSKey when the host provides
	a clock input that goes low when the chip enters deep sleep.
	Otherwise there is a significant peformance impact as the chip
	is woken unnecessarily. 
	
	On chips from BlueCore3-ROM but before BlueCore4-ROM, the key is also 
	only useful with host transports that do not use 
	PSKEY_UART_SLEEP_TIMEOUT as the chip stays awake for that period if 
	woken by a host clock. This is likely to be a source of considerable
	inefficiency. On chips from BlueCore4-ROM, the firmware distinguishies
	wakeups caused by the presence of the host clock from those caused by
	data on the UART, so this restriction does not apply.
	
	Casual scanning is not used in continuous page scan, because in this
	case the chip never becomes inactive.
	
	If casual scanning is in use, the link manager reports the
	scan repetition mode based on the larger of the page scan interval
	and the casual scan interval.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_AFH_MIN_MAP_CHANGE (0x010b)

SUMMARY
	The minimum amount to change an AFH map by

TYPE
	uint16[2]

DEFAULT VALUE
	{ 2, 4 }

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey defines the minimum amount by which the device changes a
	channel map. If the channel map is rapidly changing by only a very
	small amount then the device prefers not to send too many channel map
	changes of classification reports.
	
	The first number is the number of channels that must have got worse to
	cause the device to send a message. The second number is the number
	of channels that must have improved to cause the device to send a
	message. Having the second number bigger than the first means that the
	device will send messages more frequently as things become worse (as
	it knocks out more channels). The device then only adds channels
	back in as things become better.
	
	Setting either value to zero disables this feature - the device
	sends the channel map message whenever the channel map changes.
	
	The 'all good' channel map is a special case: the device always
	sends this.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_LP_RUN_PERIOD (0x010c)

SUMMARY
	AFH RSSI reading period when in low power mode

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(50)

MAXIMUM
	(0xFFFF)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(5000)

DESCRIPTION
	The value of this PSKey is used in place of PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_RUN_PERIOD
	when all Bluetooth links are in a "low power" mode (see the
	description of PSKEY_AFH_OPTIONS for the definition of "low power").
	Therefore, this key is normally much larger than 
	PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_RUN_PERIOD to reduce power when links are in sniff or 
	park.
	
	This period is enabled by Bit 6 in PSKEY_AFH_OPTIONS.
	The value of this PSKey is in unit of ms.

	PSKEY_HCI_LMP_LOCAL_VERSION (0x010d)

SUMMARY

TYPE

	(0)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x0707)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the HCI_version and LMP_version information reported
	to the local host when the host sends
	HCI_Read_Local_Version_Information. The HCI_Version is the top 8 bits,
	the LMP_Version is the bottom 8 bits.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_CONDITIONAL_SCAN_BACKOFF_TIME (0x010f)

SUMMARY
	Conditional scan backoff time

TYPE
	TIME

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(1073741824)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(30000000)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the period in microseconds for which conditional
	scanning is disabled when the leaky bucket reaches
	PSKEY_CONDITIONAL_SCAN_BACKOFF_LEVEL. See that PSKey's description for
	how the leaky bucket works.
	
	The firmware also stops conditional scanning for this period when it
	receives an inquiry or when the last connection has just ended,
	returning the firmware to the idle state. Conditional scanning is
	never performed in the connected state.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_CONDITIONAL_SCAN_BUCKET_BOTTOM (0x0110)

SUMMARY
	Conditional scan leaky bucket bottom

TYPE
	int8

MINIMUM
	(-126)

MAXIMUM
	(0)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(-10)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey value provides a clip on the minimum level of the leaky 
	bucket used to manage the power use of the conditional scan. The
	closer this value is to zero, the less a history of radio inactivity
	matters when deciding whether to conditional scan.
	
	See the description of PSKEY_CONDITIONAL_SCAN_BACKOFF_LEVEL for a
	description of the leaky bucket mechanism.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_CONDITIONAL_SCAN_BUCKET_BACKOFF_LEVEL (0x0111)

SUMMARY
	Conditional scan leaky bucket backoff level

TYPE
	int8

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(127)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(10)

DESCRIPTION
	When using conditional scan, if the radio environment is busy,
	performing the conditional scan plus the ordinary page/inquiry scan
	uses more power than conditional scan alone. To turn off
	conditional scan when the radio environment is busy, the LM uses a
	leaky bucket filter.
	
	The bucket level is incremented by 1 whenever the conditional scan
	detected a radio source, and decremented by an amount that depends on
	the scan window and interval when the conditional scan did not detect
	a radio source. The decrement amount is calculated to keep the level
	at zero at the percentage chance of radio activity where conditional
	scanning uses an equal amount of power to not conditional scanning.
	When the level rises above zero, it is becoming inefficient to
	conditional scan. When the level goes below zero (possible as the
	level is a signed value), it is more efficient to conditional scan
	than not to.
	
	When the bucket level reaches the value of this PSKey, conditional
	scanning is disabled for the period of time given by
	PSKEY_CONDITIONAL_SCAN_BACKOFF_TIME. It is then re-enabled with the
	bucket level set back to zero.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_CONDITIONAL_SCAN_BACK_TO_BACK_OPTIMISE (0x0112)

SUMMARY
	Conditional scan back to back optimisation

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(TRUE)

DESCRIPTION
	When page scan and inquiry scan have the same interval, to save power
	the scans are done back-to-back, with inquiry scan first and
	then page scan. When this PSKey is True, if the inquiry scan was a
	conditional scan and the conditional scan heard nothing, the following
	page scan is not performed. Conversely, if the inquiry scan was a
	conditional scan and heard something, the following page scan is never
	a conditional scan, but always an ordinary page scan. This PSKey is
	best used when the scan window is short compared to the scan interval.
	
	When this key is False, the conditional scanning from page and inquiry
	are not coupled in this way, although both still contribute to the
	leaky bucket which decides whether to conditional scan.
	
	This PSKey only has an effect if conditional scan is enabled using
	PSKEY_CONDITIONAL_SCAN_ENABLE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_ERROR_CODE_LTADDR_EXHAUSTION (0x0114)

SUMMARY
	Error code to be used when we run out of LT_ADDRs

TYPE
	uint8

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x09)

DESCRIPTION
	The BlueTooth specification is not clear about which HCI
	error code should be used if a device runs out of LT addresses when
	it has fewer than the maximum allowed number of ACL connections (see
	PSKEY_MAX_ACLS). This can happen if a connection is lost without a
	clean disconnect taking place; the device then reserves the
	address that the connection was using for some amount of time.
	
	If an attempt is made to create an ACL connection, for example
	to perform a remote name request or service search, when the device
	has fewer than PSKEY_MAX_ACLS existing ACL connections but has no
	available LT_ADDRs, the value of this PSKey is returned in the HCI
	command complete event. 
	
	Note: The value of this key does not get validated at all. However, 
	CSR recommends only using the following values:
	
	- Connection Limit Exceeded (0x09)
	  This is the same error code as that returned if PSKEY_MAX_ACLS is
	  exceeded. Because this value is ambiguous, it is unsuitable for some
	  hosts.
	
	- Memory Capacity Exceeded (0x07)
	  This error code is also returned if the device runs out of RAM and
	  suggests to the host that the attempt should succeed if the host
	  first performs an operation that frees up some RAM. As freeing
	  RAM does not help in the case of LT_ADDR exhaustion, this error
	  code is misleading and so unsuitable for some hosts.
	
	- Connection Rejected due to Limited Resources (0x0d)
	  This error code is meant to suggest that the connection has been
	  rejected by the remote device but, in this case, the connection
	  has been rejected by the local device so this error code is not
	  correct.
	
	- Unspecified Error (0x1f)
	  The most suitable of the defined error codes but not specific
	  to this error condition.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_SP_ENABLE_ECC_KEY_CHANGES (0x0115)

SUMMARY
	Enable ECC key protection by changing keys

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(FALSE)

DESCRIPTION
	When enabled, this key will cause the BlueCore device to change the 
	public/private keypair intermittently in line with guidance from the
	Bluetooth specification.
	This provides protection against some forms of attacks on the DH key
	exchange procedure.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_SP_STORE_GENERATED_ECC_KEY (0x0116)

SUMMARY
	Store ECC keys genereted during Simple Pairing

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(FALSE)

DESCRIPTION
	If this PSKey is set to TRUE then any ECC keys generated during Simple
	Pairing are written into PSKEY_SP_ECC_KEY.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_SP_ECC_KEY (0x0117)

SUMMARY
	ECC P192 Key Pair

TYPE
	uint16[]

DEFAULT VALUE
	<none>

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets a P192 ECC Simple Pairing Key Pair. If this PSKey is
	set, BlueCore will not generate a key pair but instead use the one 
	provided in this PSKey. 
	The valid format is as follows:
	[private key length][private key][public key X length][public key X]
	[public key Y length][public key Y]
	
	where X and Y are the first and second halves of the public key 
	respectively. The length fields specify the number of used words
	in the respective key field (i.e. after stripping MS zero words) -
	The actual size of the fields are fixed.
	
	The keys should be split into 16-bit words and programmed least
	significant word first. 
	
	For example, a 32-bit key: 0791 5f86
	
	becomes: 5f86 0791 
	
	It is important that this template must be followed exactly otherwise 
	the PSKey will be disregarded with no warning or error message 
	returned.
	
	Warning: Setting this key to the debug values as specified by the
	Bluetooth Core Specification is considered insecure as an 
	active/passive attacker that has access to the debug private key
	can proceed to eavesdrop on all encrypted traffic between the hosts 
	and perform a Man-in-the-Middle attack.
	
	This key should only be altered on the advice of CSR.
	
	If PSKEY_SP_STORE_GENERATED_ECC_KEY is set to TRUE then any generated
	key pairs will be written to this PSKey.
	
	There is a PSKEY_SP_ECC_P256_KEY which is the equivalent of this PSKey
	but for storage of P256 key pairs. 
	The two keys are not dependent on one another.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_BLE_VERSION_IND_RATE (0x011b)

SUMMARY
	Sets the rate for BLE version exchange

TYPE
	uint8

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(30)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(10)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey determines the likelihood of version exchange being done
	automatically when Bluetooth Low Energy (BLE) connections are made.
	If the value of the key is n then version exchange is done
	automatically every n connections.
	If set to zero (the default), no automatic version exchange takes
	place.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_DEFAULT_BLE_FEATURES (0x011c)

SUMMARY
	BLE local supported features

TYPE
	uint16[4]

DEFAULT VALUE
	{ 0x0001, 0x0000, 0x0000, 0x0000 }

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey contains a 4-element array of uint16s holding a bitfield
	that describes the Bluetooth Low Energy (BLE) features supported by
	the local device.
	
	Currently only the first word is being used (from the LSB upwards) 
	as defined in the BLE feature set as per the specification. The
	remaining bits are currently unused.
	
	The PSKey's default value gives the firmware's capabilities. Switching
	a bit from 0 to 1 does not create a missing capability.
	
	This PSKey configures the local LM. If a feature is marked as provided
	by the default value, then clearing the PSKey's bit turns off the
	corresponding functionality. For example, setting the Encryption bit
	to zero stops the local device supporting encryption.
	
	The bit order as per the specification is:
	
	First word, low to high
	  Bit     Feature
	  0       LE Encryption
	  1       Connection Parameters Request Procedure
	  2       Extended Reject Indication
	  3       Slave-initiated Features Exchange
	  [15:4]  RFU
	
	Second word
	         [15:0]  RFU
	
	Third word
	         [15:0]  RFU
	
	Fourth word
	         [15:0]  RFU
	

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_BLE_FEATURE_REQ_RATE (0x011d)

SUMMARY
	Sets the rate for a BLE master to send an autonomous feature request

TYPE
	uint8

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(30)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(10)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey determines the likelihood of feature exchange being done
	automatically when Bluetooth Low Energy (BLE) connections are made.
	If the value of the key is n then feature exchange is done
	automatically every n connections.
	If set to zero (the default), no automatic feature exchange takes
	place.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_BLE_SUPPORTED_STATES (0x011e)

SUMMARY
	LE supported states and state combinations

TYPE
	uint16[4]

DEFAULT VALUE
	{0xFFFF, 0x1FFF, 0x0000, 0x0000}

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds a 4-element array of uint16s holding a bitfield that 
	defines the Bluetooth Low Energy (BLE) states and state combinations 
	supported by the local device.
	
	Currently only the first 29 bits are used (from the LSB 
	upwards) as defined in the LE_States. The remaining bits are 
	currently unused (set to all 0s)
	
	The PSKey's default value gives the states and state combinations that
	the firmware supports. This PSKey does not configure the firmware to 
	support states or state combinations. It should be updated if 
	the states or state combinations supported changes from the default. 
	This PSKey is used only for information purposes.
	
	The bit order (LSB to MSB) as per the specification is.
	
	  Bit set Description
	  none    No state combinations supported  
	  0       Non-connectable advertising state supported  
	  1       Discoverable advertising state supported  
	  2       Connectable advertising state supported  
	  3       Directed advertising state supported  
	  4       Passive scanning state supported  
	  5       Active scanning state supported 
	  6       Initiating state supported
	          Connection state in the master role also supported 
	  7       Connection state in the slave role supported  
	  8       Non-connectable advertising state and passive scanning state
	          combination supported.  
	  9       Discoverable advertising state and passive scanning state
	          combination supported.  
	  10      Connectable advertising state and passive scanning state
	          combination supported.  
	  11      Directed advertising state and passive scanning state
	          combination supported.
	  12      Non-connectable advertising state and active scanning state
	          combination supported.  
	  13      Discoverable advertising state and active scanning state
	          combination supported.  
	  14      Connectable advertising state and active scanning state
	          combination supported.  
	  15      Directed advertising state and active scanning state
	          combination supported.
	  16      Non-connectable advertising state and initiating state
	          combination supported.
	  17      Discoverable advertising state and initiating state
	          combination supported.
	  18      Non-connectable advertising state and master role
	          combination supported.
	  19      Discoverable advertising state and master role
	          combination supported.
	  20      Non-connectable advertising state and slave role 
	          combination supported.
	  21      Discoverable advertising state and slave role 
	          combination supported.
	  22      Passive scanning state and initiating state combination 
	          supported.
	  23      Active scanning state and initiating state combination 
	          supported.
	  24      Passive scanning state and master role combination
	          supported
	  25      Active scanning state and master role combination
	          supported
	  26      Passive scanning state and slave role combination
	          supported
	  27      Active scanning state and slave role combination
	          supported
	  28      Initiating state and master role combination supported
	          Master role and master role combination also supported
	  29      Low duty cycle directed advertising supported
	  30      Low duty cycle directed advertising and passive scanning
	          state combination supported
	  31      Low duty cycle directed advertising and active scanning
	          state combination supported
	  32      Connectable advertising state, initiating state, and
	          simultaneous master & slave role combination supported
	  33      Directed advertising state, initiating state, and
	          simultaneous master & slave role combination supported
	  34      Low duty cycle directed advertising, initiating state,
	          and simultaneous master & slave role combination supported
	  35      Connectable advertising state, master role, and 
	          simultaneous master & slave role combination supported
	  36      Directed advertising state, master role, and simultaneous
	          master & slave role combination supported
	  37      Low duty cycle directed advertising, master role, and 
	          simultaneous master & slave role combination supported
	  38      Connectable advertising state, slave role, and simultaneous
	          slave role & slave role combination supported
	  39      Directed advertising state, slave role, and simultaneous
	          slave role & slave role combination supported
	  40      Low duty cycle directed advertising, slave role, and 
	          simultaneous slave role & slave role combination supported
	  41      Initiating state, slave role, and simultaneous master & 
	          slave role combination supported
	  [63:42] RFU
	   

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_AFH_BLE_MIN_MAP_CHANGE (0x011f)

SUMMARY
	The minimum amount to change a BLE AFH map by

TYPE
	uint16[2]

DEFAULT VALUE
	{ 2, 4 }

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey defines the minimum amount that the device changes
	the BLE channel map when it is the master of a connection. If the
	channel map is rapidly changing by only a very small amount then the
	device prefers not to send too many channel map updates to the slave.
	
	The first value is the number of channels that must have worsened to
	cause the device to send a message. The second value is the number
	of channels that must have improved to cause the device to send a
	message. Having the second number bigger than the first means that
	the device sends messages more frequently as things become worse
	(as it knocks out more channels), and less frequently as things
	become better (minimising false positives).
	
	Setting either value to zero disables this feature. The device
	sends the channel map message every time the channel map changes.
	
	The 'all good' channel map is a special case: the device always
	sends this.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_BLE_MAX_ADVERT_FILTERS (0x0120)

SUMMARY
	The maximum number of filters on BLE adverts.

TYPE
	uint8

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(255)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(3)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey defines the absolute maximum number of advert filters that
	can be set by either a VM application or by using the bccmd 
	ble_adv_filt_add interface. 
	
	It acts as a safeguard against excessive memory usage, but does not
	explicitly commit memory to filters.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_BLE_SLAVE_ALLOW_BREDR (0x0121)

SUMMARY
	Allow BLE slaves to partake in BR/EDR activities.

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(FALSE)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey controls internal link manager behaviour. Do not change
	it except on specific advice from CSR.
	This PSKey exists to disable specific BLE and  BR/EDR role
	combinations that are prohibited by the Generic Access Profile.
	Enabling this PSKey will allow the prohibited role combinations,
	which will potentially allow BLE links to clash with BR/EDR links
	with unpredictable results and possible loss of throughput.

NAME
	PSKEY_DFU_ATTRIBUTES (0x0136)

SUMMARY
	DFU attributes

TYPE
	uint8

DEFAULT VALUE
	(7)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the bmAttributes field of the run-time DFU Functional 
	Descriptor, as defined in Table 4.2 of USB DFU specification 1.0.
	
	The default value (7) means "manifest tolerant, upload + download 
	capable."
	
	This applies for the USB and "DFU over UART" (protocol name not yet
	allocated) protocols.

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(5000)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the wDetachTimeOut field of the run-time DFU
	Functional Descriptor, as defined in Table 4.2 of USB DFU
	specification 1.0.
	
	The value is in milliseconds.
	
	This applies for the USB and "DFU over UART" (protocol name not yet

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_DFU_TRANSFER_SIZE (0x0138)

SUMMARY
	DFU transfer size

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(1023)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the wTransferSize field of the run-time DFU 
	Functional Descriptor, as defined in Table 4.2 of USB DFU 
	specification 1.0. This PSKey applies to all - "DFU over USB-DFU 
	class", "DFU over USB-HID class" and "DFU over UART" (protocol name
	not yet allocated) protocols.
	
	The maximum permissible value for this PSKey is 1023 (0x3FF) for all
	transports. (This limit is imposed by the USB hardware). The default
	value (1023) is in bytes.
	Note: The BCSP size may be overridden (by a smaller value) at low 
	baud rates.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_DFU_ENABLE (0x0139)

SUMMARY
	DFU enable

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(TRUE)

DESCRIPTION
	If TRUE this PSKey enables the use of DFU. I.e. support for DFU is
	advertised in the USB descriptors and DFU commands are
	processed. Otherwise support for the protocol is not
	advertised and DFU commands are rejected.
	
	This PSKey applies to both the USB and "DFU over UART" (protocol name
	not yet allocated) protocols. It is intended for use in countries
	such as Japan where firmware upgrades may not be allowed for radio
	devices.
	
	Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to
	FALSE and TRUE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_DFU_VERSION (0x013b)

SUMMARY
	USB DFU version

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x0101)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the bcdDFUVersion field of the run-time DFU functional
	descriptor as defined in table 4.2 of version 1.1 of the DFU 
	specification.
	
	This PSKey also controls the format of the functional descriptor
	(length). As described in table 4.2 of version 1.0 of the DFU
	specification, if it is 0x0100 (1.0) then a DFU 1.0 functional 
	descriptor is sent. If it is another value then a DFU 1.1 functional
	descriptor is sent.
