==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_BCSP_LM_PS_BLOCK (0x0192)

SUMMARY
	BCSP link establishment block

TYPE
	BCSP_LM_PS_BLOCK

DEFAULT VALUE
	{ 
                        1,      /* 1 to enable link sync. */ 
                        0,      /* Continuous sync packets. */ 
                        250     /* Tshy is 250ms. */ }

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey configures the BCSP link establishment protocol. This is 
	only used if BCSP is used over the chip's UART.
	
	The configuration uses a structure of type BCSP_LM_PS_BLOCK where 
	fields are:
	
	      uint16  mode           0:  disable link establishment.
	                             1:  enable link establishment.
	                             2:  enable passive-start link
	                                 establishment.  This option causes
	                                 the link establishment engine on the
	                                 device to emit no messages until it
	                                 receives traffic from the host.  
	
	      uint16  sync_retries   Support for this argument has been
	                             removed.
	
	                             It used to set the number of sync
	                             packets emitted before the BCSP
	                             link establishment engine gave up
	                             and marked the link as dead.  A
	                             value of zero meant "don't stop."
	                             The BCSP link establishment engine
	                             now always behaves as if the value
	                             is zero.
	
	      uint16  tshy           The Tshy value in milliseconds.
	
	                             This is the interval in which the BCSP
	                             link establishment engines send "sync"
	                             messages.  This value is also used by the
	                             BCSP link establishment engine's
	                             Tconf timer.
	
	For more information see CSR document "BCSP Link Establishment
	Protocol", CS-101681-SP.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_PROTOCOL_INFO0 (0x0194)

SUMMARY
	Host transport channel 0 settings (BCSP ACK)

TYPE
	PROTOCOL_INFO

DEFAULT VALUE
	{ 
                        0,      /* max_tx_payload_size. */ 
                        FALSE,  /* reliable_stream. */ 
                        0,      /* priority. */ 
                        0       /* unused - must be 0. */ }

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey configures the protocol that flows over BCSP channel 0.
	
	The host transport subsystem provides 16 channels, each of which is
	configured by a PROTOCOL_INFO struct held in the persistent store.
	
	BCSP channel 0 is dedicated to signalling between BCSP stacks, 
	specifically to carry message acknowledgements. Therefore, it is not
	available as a channel to carry user messages through BCSP, and is 
	used by the BCSP host transport only.  
	
	While channel 0 is not available, the structure described below is
	used for the other channels in the host transport subsystem.
	
	The type PROTOCOL_INFO has the following fields:
	
	        uint16 max_tx_payload_size - The maximum size in bytes of
	                BCSP payload sent to the host.  For ACL and SCO the
	                actual maximum size will be the lower of the value
	                from PS and the value indicated to the BlueCore 
	                device in the host's HOST_BUFFER_SIZE command, if one 
	                has been received.  These values are checked at run
	                time against the size of hardware buffer allocated.
	
	        int:1 reliable_stream - TRUE (bit value of 1) if the protocol 
	                uses BCSP's reliable stream.
	
	        int:4 priority - A value between 0 and 7.  Lower values
	                have higher priority.  The priority is used by the
	                device's BCSP scheduler when deciding what data to
	                send to the host.
	
	        int:1 enabled - TRUE (bit value of 1) if the protocol is 
	                enabled. The current design of the firmware code 
	                requires each protocol to be enabled explicitly 
	                internally by the firmware, so this flag should 
	                always be FALSE.
	
	The last three fields are packed as bitfields in the second word, as 
	shown below:
	
	      Bits
	       [9:0]    Unused (second byte plus lower 2 bits)
	       10       enabled
	       [14:11]  priority
	       15       reliable_stream
	
	For more information, see CSR document "BCSP Channel Allocation",
	CS-101680-SP.   

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_PROTOCOL_INFO1 (0x0195)

SUMMARY
	Host transport channel 1 settings (BCSP-LE)

TYPE
	PROTOCOL_INFO

DEFAULT VALUE
	{ 
                        256,    /* max_tx_payload_size. */ 
                        FALSE,  /* reliable_stream. */ 
                        0,      /* priority. */ 
                        0       /* unused - must be zero. */ }

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey configures the protocol that flows over BCSP channel 1. 
	This channel carries BCSP link establishment if BCSP is used. This
	channel is used only when BCSP is the host transport, however the
	max_tx_packet_size and priority settings for this protocol are also
	applied to non DFU USB traffic transmitted over the Control
	endpoint when BlueCore is using the USB host interface.
	
	
	The protocol is configured with a PROTOCOL_INFO structure. The
	structure is described with PSKEY_HOSTIO_PROTOCOL_INFO0.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_UART_RESET_TIMEOUT (0x01a4)

SUMMARY
	UART reset counter timeout

TYPE
	TIME

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(10 * SECOND)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey configures the UART's reset counter timeout in
	microseconds.
	
	If the UART's receive data line is held low for this period then the
	chip's (hardware) resets itself. Accuracy is +/- 30%, so it is
	important to specify to the nearest microsecond. 
	
	If this value is zero then the feature is disabled.
	
	Values between 1 and 999 are treated as zero.
	
	This feature only works with the UART host transports: BCSP, H4, H5
	and VM access to the UART.
	
	If PSKEY_HOSTIO_UART_RESET_TIMEOUT is set then make sure
	PSKEY_UART_BITRATE or PSKEY_UART_BAUDRATE is set to a non-zero value.
	Otherwise the chip will try autobaud detect and it will not move
	to deep sleep until UART_BREAK is removed.
	
	Type TIME is fundamentally a uint32.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_USE_HCI_EXTN (0x01a5)

SUMMARY
	Use hci_extn to route non-hci channels

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(FALSE)

DESCRIPTION
	If the system is using BCSP and this PSKey is FALSE then the non-HCI
	BCSP channels (currently 7: BCCMD, HQ, 4 higher layer access libs and
	the VM's channel) are routed via their BCSP channels. Otherwise, they
	are routed via hci_extn, described in CSR document "BlueCore HCI 
	Extensions", CS-101682-SP, available from the CSR support website.
	
	If the system is using H4 or USB then these channels are always
	routed over hci_extn.
	(Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to
	FALSE and TRUE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_USE_HCI_EXTN_CCFC (0x01a6)

SUMMARY
	Use command-complete flow control for hci_extn

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(FALSE)

DESCRIPTION
	If the system is using hci_extn to carry the non-HCI channels (see
	the description of PSKEY_HOSTIO_USE_HCI_EXTN) and this key is TRUE
	then the chip emits an "hci command complete event" for each HCI
	manufacturer extension command.
	
	Set this PSKey to TRUE so that the host->chip data flow through
	hci_extn fits most closely to the HCI flow control model. However,
	this also means the hci_extn channel has glacial performance. If this
	is FALSE then the hci_extn traffic depends (only) on the tunnelled
	channels' own flow control mechanisms.
	
	Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to
	FALSE and TRUE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_HCI_EXTN_PAYLOAD_SIZE (0x01a7)

SUMMARY
	Maximum hci_extn payload size

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(2)

MAXIMUM
	(255)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(255)

DESCRIPTION
	If the system is using hci_extn to carry the non-HCI channels (see
	the description of PSKEY_HOSTIO_USE_HCI_EXTN) then this value
	specifies the maximum size of the HCI event payloads when primitives
	on non-HCI channels are fragmented. This PSKey value is the size of 
	the HCI event payload, where one byte is used for the HCI-extn 
	payload descriptor. Therefore each fragment is, at most, one byte less
	than this value. The minimum value for this PS value is therefore 2,
	though such a low value is likely to give extremely poor
	performance. The maximum value is 255 (because the length field in
	the HCI event header is only 8 bits wide).
	
	Set this value lower than the maximum expected payload size to
	force hci_extn to fragment. This can be good when the host
	connection carries time-critical traffic, notably SCO.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_BCSP_LM_CNF_CNT_LIMIT (0x01aa)

SUMMARY
	BCSP link establishment conf message count

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(20)

DESCRIPTION
	The value of this PSKey is only used if PSKEY_USE_OLD_BCSP_LE is
	set to TRUE.
	
	Most early versions of the BCSP Link Establishment engine detected
	only that the peer BCSP stack had started - this is what the protocol
	was designed to do, as the protocol was written to support a host and
	BlueCore01 on the same circuit board (in a cell phone).
	
	Later versions of the BCSP Link Establishment engine use an extension
	that allows the local engine to spot when the peer engine restarts -
	typically the case when the peer reboots.
	
	To use this feature both sides of the BCSP link must support this
	extension and the value of this variable must be non-zero. This
	variable sets the number of "conf" messages emitted by the local
	engine, as described in CSR document "BCSP Link Establishment 
	Protocol", CS-101681-SP, available from the CSR support website.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM (0x01ab)

SUMMARY
	Map SCO over PCM

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(FALSE)

DESCRIPTION
	The following options are available to route SCO data over PCM port:
	
	- Use the BCCMD command MAP_SCO_PCM to cause the next HCI 
	  Add_SCO_Connection command to route to a PCM port.
	      
	- Use this PSKey.
	
	- [unified-25 onwards] Use streams interface.
	
	If this PSKey is TRUE and PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_CODEC is FALSE
	then all attempts to open SCO connections map to one of the PCM ports 
	based on PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM_SLOT.
	
	In HCI 14.X builds, only a single SCO stream can flow over the
	BlueCore2-EXT's PCM port.
	
	In HCI 15.X and later builds which do not have facility of 
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM_SLOT, set the PSKey to cause all attempts
	to open SCO channels to run over *the first* PCM channel in the PCM
	port. (The clock settings in PSKEY_PCM_CONFIG32 determine whether
	the PCM port can carry more than one SCO channel.)
	
	See PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM_SLOT, PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_CODEC.
	Also see the CSR document "BlueCore Audio API Specification",
	CS-209064-DD.
	
	Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to
	FALSE and TRUE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_BREAK_POLL_PERIOD (0x01ad)

SUMMARY
	Break poll period (microseconds)

TYPE
	TIME

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(10 * SECOND)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the rate at which to poll the UART at start up to 
	determine if the host is sending a break (continuous 0) in 
	microseconds. Between polls the chip enters a low power state (deep 
	sleep). If the break signal is removed, normal operation resumes.
	
	Use this PSKey with PSKEY_HOSTIO_UART_RESET_TIMEOUT. This enables 
	the host to force the chip into a low power state using a limited 
	number of I/O lines.
	
	To place the chip in a low power state, the host sends a continuous
	break which forces a hardware reset if PSKEY_HOSTIO_UART_RESET_TIMEOUT
	is set. After resetting, if the break is still present, the chip
	enters a low power state, waking only at the rate defined by this
	key to check for the continuing presence of the break.
	
	A short delay (of a few hundred microseconds) occurs after the
	reset before the low power state is entered. This is due to the time
	required to initialise the PS and the support for deep sleep. 
	
	If this value is zero then the feature is disabled.
	
	This feature only works with the BCSP, H4 and H5 host transports.
	
	Type TIME is fundamentally a uint32.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_MIN_UART_HCI_SCO_SIZE (0x01ae)

SUMMARY
	Minimum SCO packet size sent to host over UART HCI

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(1)

MAXIMUM
	(128)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(30)

DESCRIPTION
	A SCO link provides a steady flow of audio samples from air that
	have to be sent to the host. When SCO data is passed to the host
	over HCI (i.e., not over the chip's PCM port) the samples have to be
	formed into HCI SCO packets.
	
	This PSKey sets the minimum number of *samples* in each HCI SCO
	packet sent to the host over a UART transport - BCSP and H4. (USB
	has separate rules for defining SCO transport.)
	
	Set this to zero to minimise audio data latency. However this can
	crowd other data off the host transport. When the available host
	bandwidth is too low this can block all other traffic, so HCI ACL,
	HCI CMD/EVT, etc. stop flowing.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_CODEC (0x01b0)

SUMMARY
	Map SCO over the built-in codec

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(FALSE)

DESCRIPTION
	Some versions of BlueCore include an audio codec, typically used to
	drive an external microphone and earpiece.  
	
	If this PSKey is TRUE, and if PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM is also TRUE,
	then all SCO connections are routed through the built-in audio codec
	rather than though the normal PCM interface.
	
	Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to
	FALSE and TRUE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_PCM_CVSD_TX_HI_FREQ_BOOST (0x01b1)

SUMMARY
	High frequency boost for PCM when transmitting CVSD

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(4)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey enables a high-frequency emphasis filter used when 
	transmitting voice samples over the radio using CVSD (only used when 
	the host interface is the PCM interface).
	
	Do not alter the default value (disabled) of this PSKey except with 
	specific advice from CSR. Use of this PSKey is deprecated. It 
	will be removed in a future release of the firmware.
	
	A value of 0 disables the filter.  Higher values provide increasing
	amounts of high frequency boost.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_PCM_CVSD_RX_HI_FREQ_BOOST (0x01b2)

SUMMARY
	High frequency boost for PCM when receiving CVSD

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(4)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey enables a high-frequency emphasis filter used when
	receiving voice samples over the radio using CVSD (only used when the
	host interface is the PCM interface).
	
	Do not alter the default value (disabled) of this PSKey except with 
	specific advice from CSR. Use of this PSKey is deprecated. It
	will be removed in a future release of the firmware.
	
	A value of 0 disables the filter.  Higher values provide increasing
	amounts of high frequency boost.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_PCM_CONFIG32 (0x01b3)

SUMMARY
	PCM interface settings bitfields

TYPE
	uint32

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x00800000)

DESCRIPTION
	PSKEY_PCM_CONFIG is only used in BlueCore01b firmware.  
	PSKEY_PCM_CONFIG32 is used in firmware for BlueCore2 and later
	devices.
	
	This PSKey has a complex bitfield value that is described in the 
	Data Sheet for each BlueCore device. 
	
	See PSKEY_PCM_USE_LOW_JITTER_MODE for more PCM configuration options.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_USE_OLD_BCSP_LE (0x01b4)

SUMMARY
	Use the old version of BCSP link establishment

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	FALSE

DESCRIPTION
	If this PS Key is set to FALSE then the firmware uses the BCSP Link
	Establishment protocol described in CSR document "BCSP Link
	Establishment Protocol", CS-101681-SP, otherwise it uses the older
	protocol described in CSR document bc01-s-010g.
	
	The new protocol was modified to provide a more robust behavior when 
	a host spontaneously reboots or restarts. The new behavior only 
	differs significantly from the old one in that:
	
	    - The "choke" is turned off when moving from "curious" to
	      "garrulous".
	
	    - The "cnf_cnt_limit" logic is removed; "conf" messages are
	      continuously emitted in the "curious" state.
	
	For detailed descriptions of the state machines and signals see CSR
	document "BCSP Link Establishment Protocol", CS-101681-SP.
	
	You may need to set this PSKey to TRUE if the host has an old 
	implementation of BCSP Link Establishment. Old implementations
	may not support the "garrulous" state.
	
	See PSKEY_BCSP_LM_CNF_CNT_LIMIT.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_PCM_FORMAT (0x01b6)

SUMMARY
	PCM data format

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x006c)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the data format used to send SCO data over the PCM
	port. The format is the same as for HCI_Write_Voice_Setting. The
	bottom two bits of this key (air format) are always ignored and should
	be set to zero. The air format specified with HCI_Write_Voice_Setting
	is used instead.
	
	The Bluetooth HCI spec mandates that devices boot up with 16-bit
	linear data format. Unfortunately many PCM codecs do not expect this
	format so this PSKey allows the HCI format to be overridden so that
	manufacturers can set it correctly for the hardware and application
	designers do not need to know the correct format.
	
	If this PSKey is set to 0xffff then the format specified
	with HCI_Write_Voice_Settings is used and so the PCM format
	can be changed dynamically (this is almost never required).
	
	On BlueCore2 all PCM streams get the same format.
	
	On devices with an internal codec, if SCO data is routed to the
	internal codec then this PSKey is ignored and the correct value for
	the internal codec is used.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_CODEC_OUT_GAIN (0x01b7)

SUMMARY
	Audio output gain when using built-in codec

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(0xFFFF)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x0007)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the audio output gain when using the built-in codec.
	
	The interpretation varies depending on the device.
	
	BlueCore2-External: 
	 Bits [2:0] set the gain (7 = maximum gain)
	
	BlueCore5-MM:
	 Bits [2:0] set the analogue gain (5 = unity gain)
	 Bits [7:4] set the digital gain (0 = unity gain)
	 Bit [10] enables an extra 3dB of gain on DAC_A
	 Bit [11] enables an extra 3dB of gain on DAC_B
	
	BlueCore7-MM:
	 Bits [2:0] set the analogue gain (7 = unity gain)
	 Bits [7:4] set the digital gain (0 = unity gain)
	
	On other devices with a codec:
	 Bits [2:0] set the analogue gain (5 = unity gain)
	 Bits [7:4] set the digital gain (0 = unity gain)
	 Bits [9:8] set the sigma-delta gain (0 = nominal)
	
	Important exception:
	 On BlueCore7-FM the codec ADC and DAC share the same analogue gain.
	 Therefore bits [2:0] also set the codec analogue input gain.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_CODEC_IN_GAIN (0x01b8)

SUMMARY
	Audio input gain when using built-in codec

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(0xFFFF)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x0108)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the audio input gain when using the built-in codec.
	
	The interpretation varies depending on the device.
	
	BlueCore2 External: 
	 Bits [3:0] set the gain (0xF = maximum)
	
	BlueCore3-MM and BlueCore5-MM:
	 Bits   [3:0] set the analogue gain    (8 = optimum noise)
	 Bits   [7:4] set the digital gain     (0 = unity gain)
	
	BlueCore7-MM:
	 Bits   [3:0] set the analogue gain (1 = unity gain)
	 Bits   [7:4] set the digital gain (0 = unity gain)
	 Bit    [8]   enables the input pre-amplifier
	 Bits   [9:10] set the pre-amplifier gain (0 = unity gain)
	
	On other devices with a codec:
	 Bits   [3:0] set the analogue gain    (8 = optimum noise)
	 Bits   [7:4] set the digital gain     (0 = unity gain)
	 Bit      [8] enables scaling down of DAC outputs
	
	Important exception:
	 On BlueCore7-FM, the codec ADC uses the same analogue gain as the DAC
	 Therefore bits [3:0] are ignored on BlueCore7-FM.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_CODEC_PIO (0x01b9)

SUMMARY
	PIO to enable when built-in codec is enabled

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	<none>

ENUM_INCLUDE_FILE
	io_bt.h

ENUM_VALUES
	                MIC_BIAS_PIO_0   Use PIO 0
	                MIC_BIAS_PIO_1   Use PIO 1
	                MIC_BIAS_PIO_2   Use PIO 2
	                MIC_BIAS_PIO_3   Use PIO 3
	                MIC_BIAS_PIO_4   Use PIO 4
	                MIC_BIAS_PIO_5   Use PIO 5
	                MIC_BIAS_PIO_6   Use PIO 6
	                MIC_BIAS_PIO_7   Use PIO 7
	                MIC_BIAS_PIO_8   Use PIO 8
	                MIC_BIAS_PIO_9   Use PIO 9
	               MIC_BIAS_PIO_10   Use PIO 10
	               MIC_BIAS_PIO_11   Use PIO 11
	               MIC_BIAS_PIO_12   Use PIO 12
	               MIC_BIAS_PIO_13   Use PIO 13
	               MIC_BIAS_PIO_14   Use PIO 14
	               MIC_BIAS_PIO_15   Use PIO 15
	              MIC_BIAS_AUX_DAC   Use AUX_DAC pin
	MIC_BIAS_HARDWARE_MIC_BIAS_PIN   Use hardware Mic Bias pin

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the Bluecore pin to drive high when the built-in codec
	is enabled. This is typically used to bias the microphone input.
	
	When this key is not set, no PIO pin is enabled.
	
	On older BlueCore firmware selecting PIO15 instead uses AUX_DAC.
	On newer firmware (unified-23 & later) use the value MIC_BIAS_AUX_DAC
	instead.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_SCO_PCM_THRESHOLDS (0x01bb)

SUMMARY
	Thresholds for SCO PCM buffers

TYPE
	uint16[2]

DEFAULT VALUE
	{8, 20}

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the upper and lower thresholds for the buffers used to
	hold SCO data flowing between air and the PCM port.
	
	The thresholds are checked just before a packet is received from air
	and just after a packet is sent to air.
	
	If the data pending in the buffer exceeds the upper threshold when the
	level is checked, a sample is deleted from the buffer. If the pending
	data in the buffer drops below the lower threshold, a sample is
	inserted into the buffer.
	
	The thresholds are held as a uint16[2]. The first value gives the
	lower threshold and the second value gives the upper threshold.
	
	This PSKey has no effect on some versions of firmware.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_SCO_HCI_THRESHOLDS (0x01bc)

SUMMARY
	Thresholds for SCO HCI buffers

TYPE
	uint16[2]

DEFAULT VALUE
	{10, 80}

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the upper and lower thresholds for the buffers used 
	to hold SCO data flowing between air and the HCI.
	
	The thresholds are checked just before a packet is received from air
	and just after a packet is sent to air.
	
	When the thresholds are exceeded, the firmware inserts or delete
	single samples or groups of samples to bring the amount of data
	pending in the buffer into range. The exact behaviour depends on
	whether the SCO data is in transparent format and which host transport
	is in use.
	
	The thresholds are held as a uint16[2]. The first value gives the
	lower threshold and the second value gives the upper threshold.
	
	This PSKey has no effect on some versions of firmware.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM_SLOT (0x01bd)

SUMMARY
	Route SCO data to specified slot in pcm frame

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(7)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0)

DESCRIPTION
	When PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM is TRUE, the first SCO
	channel opened is routed over the chip's PCM port.  While this SCO
	channel is in place, all subsequent attempts to open extra SCO
	channels fail.
	
	The SCO channel is routed over the PCM timing frame slot defined by
	this PSKey. This PSKey's default value, zero, routes to "the first"
	PCM slot.
	
	The number of slots in the PCM port's timing frame depends on the
	value of PSKEY_PCM_CONFIG32. For example, there is no use in setting
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM_SLOT to 3, asking for SCO data to travel
	over the 4th slot in the PCM frame if the PCM channel's clock rate
	only supports a single slot per frame.
	
	This PSKey is available only in builds for BlueCore2 and later
	chips. Functionality equivalent to this PSKey is available in
	BlueCore01b builds using a bit field in PSKEY_PCM_CONFIG, a PSKey
	absent from builds for BlueCore2 and later chips.
	
	The maximum value for this PSKey is now 7 for BlueCore7-FM, where the 
	upper 4 slots redirect the PCM out of interface 2.
	
	For all previous chips the maximum value is 3.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_BCSP (0x01bf)

SUMMARY
	UART configuration when using BCSP

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x0806)

DESCRIPTION
	If PSKEY_HOST_INTERFACE selects BCSP then the UART's
	configuration register is set to the value of this PSKey when it
	boots. 
	
	The UART configuration register is a bitfield:
	
	  Bit Meaning
	    0 0 => one stop bit, 1 => two stop bits.
	    1 0 => no parity bits, 1 => one parity bit.
	    2 0 => odd parity, 1 => even parity.
	    3 0 => h/w flow control disabled, 1 => enabled.
	    4 Set to 0.
	    5 0 => RTS deasserted, 1 => RTS asserted.
	    6 Set to 0.
	    7 0 => non-BCSP/H5 operation disabled, 1 => enabled.
	    8 Set to 0.
	    9 Set to 0.
	   10 Set to 0.
	   11 Set to 1.
	   12 0 => H5 operation disabled, 1 => enabled.
	   13 Set to 0.
	   14 Set to 0.
	   15 Set to 0.
	
	The default value, 0x0806, selects BCSP mode and even parity.
	
	In builds from HCI 18.X, this key replaces PSKEY_UART_CONFIG, 
	PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_STOP_BITS, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_PARITY_BIT, 
	PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_FLOW_CTRL_EN, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_RTS, and
	PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_NON_BCSP_EN.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_H4 (0x01c0)

SUMMARY
	UART configuration when using H4

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x08a8)

DESCRIPTION
	If PSKEY_HOST_INTERFACE selects H4 then the UART's
	configuration register is set to the value of this PSKey when it
	boots. 
	
	The UART configuration register is a bitfield and shares its
	format with PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_BCSP:
	
	  Bit Meaning
	    0 0 => one stop bit, 1 => two stop bits.
	    1 0 => no parity bits, 1 => one parity bit.
	    2 0 => odd parity, 1 => even parity.
	    3 0 => h/w flow control disabled, 1 => enabled.
	    4 Set to 0.
	    5 0 => RTS deasserted, 1 => RTS asserted.
	    6 Set to 0.
	    7 0 => non-BCSP/H5 operation disabled, 1 => enabled.
	    8 Set to 0.
	    9 Set to 0.
	   10 Set to 0.
	   11 Set to 1.
	   12 0 => H5 operation disabled, 1 => enabled.
	   13 Set to 0.
	   14 Set to 0.
	   15 Set to 0.
	
	The default value, 0x08a8, selects use of hardware flow control,
	as required by the H4 specification.
	
	In builds from HCI 18.X, this key replaces PSKEY_UART_CONFIG, 
	PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_STOP_BITS, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_PARITY_BIT, 
	PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_FLOW_CTRL_EN, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_RTS, and 
	PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_NON_BCSP_EN.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_UART_TX_CRCS (0x01c3)

SUMMARY
	Use CRCs for BCSP or H5

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(TRUE)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey determines whether CRCs are used in BCSP packets sent to
	the host.
	
	This PS key is also used with H5.
	
	Note: The "H5" host transport protocol is properly known as the 
	"Three-Wire  UART Transport Layer", but is commonly known as H5 
	within CSR.
	
	In builds from HCI 18.X, this key replaces PSKEY_UART_USE_CRC_ON_TX.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_UART_ACK_TIMEOUT (0x01c4)

SUMMARY
	Acknowledgement timeout for BCSP and H5

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(250)

DESCRIPTION
	When the firmware sends a reliable message over BCSP or H5 it starts
	a timer. The timer's period is the value of this PSKey in
	milliseconds. If the host acknowledges reception of the message
	before the timer fires then the timer is cancelled. If the timer
	fires then the message is sent again and another timer started, etc.
	
	You can limit the number of times a timer is used for
	a given reliable BCSP/H5 message using PSKEY_UART_TX_MAX_ATTEMPTS.
	
	Note: The "H5" host transport protocol is properly known as the 
	"Three-Wire  UART Transport Layer", but is commonly known as H5 
	within CSR.
	
	For more information see CSR document "BlueCore Serial Protocol 
	(BCSP)", CS-101685-SP.
	
	The sleep timeout configured in PSKEY_UART_SLEEP_TIMEOUT, if enabled,
	must be greater than the acknowledgement timeout configured in this
	PSKEY.
	
	If the host wakeup mechanism is enabled with PSKEY_UART_HOST_WAKE,
	the Sleep_Delay configured in that PSKey must also be greater than
	the acknowledgement timeout configured here.
	
	In builds from HCI 18.X, this key replaces PSKEY_UART_SEQ_TIMEOUT.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_UART_TX_MAX_ATTEMPTS (0x01c5)

SUMMARY
	Max times to send reliable BCSP or H5 message

TYPE
	uint16

MAXIMUM
	(200)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0)

DESCRIPTION
	The description of PSKEY_UART_ACK_TIMEOUT outlines BCSP's mechanism
	to retransmit reliable messages to the host until acknowledged.
	
	This PSKey sets a limit on the number of
	times the send/timeout cycle is attempted. If this limit is
	reached, the firmware panics and usually reboots.
	
	Messages are sent indefinitely if this PSKey is set to zero, i.e.,
	the value zero is treated as infinity.
	
	This PSKey is also used with H5.
	
	Note: The "H5" host transport protocol is properly known as the 
	"Three-Wire  UART Transport Layer", but is commonly known as H5 
	within CSR.
	
	For more information see CSR document "BlueCore Serial Protocol 
	(BCSP)", CS-101685-SP.
	
	In builds from HCI 18.X, this key replaces PSKEY_UART_SEQ_RETRIES.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_UART_TX_WINDOW_SIZE (0x01c6)

SUMMARY
	Transmit window size for BCSP and H5

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(1)

MAXIMUM
	(6)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(4)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey holds the size of the sliding window used by BCSP.
	
	When the baseband sends a reliable BCSP message to the host then the
	host is required to acknowledge its reception. If it is not
	acknowledged within a certain period the message is sent again.
	
	The baseband sends several packets to the host before waiting for
	the first of the packets to be acknowledged. The maximum number of
	sent packets that can be unacknowledged at any time is set by this
	PSKey. When a packet is acknowledged, the next packet is sent.
	Under normal circumstances, the number of packets in transit to the
	peer is the value of PSKEY_UART_TX_WINDOW_SIZE.
	
	This PSKey is also used with H5.  
	
	Note: The "H5" host transport protocol is properly known as the 
	"Three-Wire  UART Transport Layer", but is commonly known as H5 
	within CSR.
	
	For more information see CSR document "BlueCore Serial Protocol 
	(BCSP)", CS-101685-SP.
	
	In builds from HCI 18.X, this key replaces PSKEY_UART_SEQ_WINSIZE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_UART_HOST_WAKE (0x01c7)

SUMMARY
	UART host wakeup

TYPE
	uint16[4]

DEFAULT VALUE
	{4, 		/* disable */ 
			500,            /* ms before host sleeps */ 
			10,             /* ms wakeup pulse needed */ 
			0}              /* ms pause before comms */

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey configures the use of a wakeup signal by the BlueCore to 
	wake the peer UART device from a low power state. The wakeup signal, 
	which may be either a UART break condition or a pulse on a PIO line, 
	is specified by PSKEY_UART_HOST_WAKE_SIGNAL. 
	
	If this PSKey's mechanism is turned on, the firmware judges when the
	peer may have entered its deep sleep state based on timers, and the
	local device can be set to emit a wakeup signal before sending data
	to the peer. Normally the length of the break condition is set to be
	sufficient to allow the peer to come fully awake as the local device
	normally sends a message to the peer afterwards.
	
	Most systems do not require the BlueCore to emit a wakeup signal to
	wake up the peer device. Systems using the BCSP transport, for
	example, support the host and baseband entering a deep sleep state,
	in which their UARTs are disabled. The devices may enter deep sleep
	when they choose, without warning that they are about to enter deep
	sleep and without signalling when they are in deep sleep. When one
	device wishes to send data to its peer it sends a message; the
	message can be lost (because the peer's UART may be turned off) but
	the presence of the message rouses the peer. For reliable BCSP
	channels the message is resent if it has not been acknowledged after
	a delay (set by PSKEY_UART_ACK_TIMEOUT), and the message normally
	gets through the second time, as the peer is then awake. This
	mechanism is adequate for most systems, but using a host
	wakeup signal may reduce delay implied by PSKEY_UART_ACK_TIMEOUT.
	
	This use of wakeup signals by the BlueCore is turned off by default,
	as this suits most systems.
	
	This PSKey has four uint16 parameters:
	
	    Enable: Values: 1 => enable mechanism
	                    4 => disable mechanism
	    Sleep_Delay: Milliseconds after tx to host or rx from host, after 
	                    which host is assumed to have gone into its
	                    deep sleep state. (Range 1 -> 65535.)
	                    When using BCSP or H5 host transports it is 
	                    recommended that this is greater than the
	                    acknowledge delay (set by PSKEY_UART_ACK_TIMEOUT).
	    Break_Length: Duration of wake signal in milliseconds.
	                    (Range 1 -> 1000.)
	    Pause_Length: Milliseconds between end of wake signal and
	                    sending data to the host. (Range 0 -> 1000.) 
	
	In builds from HCI 18.X, this key replaces
	PSKEY_UART_HOST_INITIAL_STATE, PSKEY_UART_HOST_ATTENTION_SPAN,
	PSKEY_UART_HOST_WAKEUP_TIME, and PSKEY_UART_HOST_WAKEUP_WAIT.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HOSTIO_THROTTLE_TIMEOUT (0x01c8)

SUMMARY
	Host interface performance control.

TYPE
	TIME

DEFAULT VALUE
	(200 * MILLISECOND)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey modifies the behaviour of the BlueCore's host interface
	code. Only configure this PSKey on specific advice from CSR.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_UART_HOST_WAKE_SIGNAL (0x01ca)

SUMMARY
	Signal to use for uart host wakeup protocol

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x0000)

DESCRIPTION
	BlueCore can be configured to output a wakeup signal to the host
	prior to sending it data if it considers that the host may be in a
	low power state. PSKEY_UART_HOST_WAKE enables this wakeup signalling
	and specifies the various timers required. 
	This PSKey specifies the wakeup signal to 
	use: a UART break signal, a pulse on a PIO line or, for the 
	H4DS transport only, a repeated byte sequence.
	
	This PSKey's value is split into two:
	  Bits [3:0] hold a value that specifies the Host Wake Mechanism.
	  Valid values are:
	                     0 - repeated byte sequence (only for H4DS)
	                     1 - positive pulse on PIO
	                     2 - negative pulse on PIO
	                     3 - UART BREAK condition
	
	  Bits [7:4] hold a value that specifies the PIO pin to be used if a
	  PIO pulse was specified as the Host Wake Mechanism.
	
	
	If the Host Wake Mechanism is 0x00, BlueCore sends a repeated
	byte sequence. The duration of the byte train is specified by
	PSKEY_H4DS_WAKE_DURATION. This mechanism is available for the H4DS
	transport only. The byte sequence has been chosen to work well with
	BlueCore's Baud rate detection capability.
	
	If 0x00 is chosen when the host transport is not H4DS a UART BREAK 
	condition is used.
	
	If the Host Wake Mechanism is 0x01 then a positive pulse is signalled
	on the PIO pin selected by Bits [7:4]. (Value 0x0 in Bits [7:4]
	selects PIO[0], value 0x01 selects PIO[1], etc.). The duration of the
	pulse is specified by PSKEY_H4DS_WAKE_DURATION for the H4DS transport
	and by PSKEY_UART_HOST_WAKE for all other host transports.
	
	If the Host Wake Mechanism is 0x02 then a negative pulse is signalled
	on the PIO pin selected by Bits [7:4]. The duration of the pulse is
	specified by PSKEY_H4DS_WAKE_DURATION for the H4DS transport, and by
	PSKEY_UART_HOST_WAKE for all other host transports.
	
	If the Host Wake Mechanism is 0x03 then a break condition is signalled
	by the UART. The duration of the break signal is specified by
	PSKEY_H4DS_WAKE_DURATION for the H4DS transport, and by
	PSKEY_UART_HOST_WAKE for all other host transports.
	
	For more information see CSR document "Host Wakeup Application Note", 
	CS-101406-An, on the CSR support website.

	Set side-tone gain

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(15)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the side-tone gain for hardware that supports
	side-tone. The higher the gain, the higher the dB value.
	On chips prior to BlueCore6, the maximum gain is 7.
	On BlueCore6 chips the maximum gain is 9.

SUMMARY
	Digital Audio Interface override for port clock rate

TYPE
	uint32

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x00000000)

DESCRIPTION
	When acting as a master on the Digital Audio Interface, typically
	using I2S or DSP mode, this PSKey allows you to define the exact
	clock rate generated, specified in Hz.
	
	If set to zero, BlueCore calculates the clock rate based
	on the sample rate and bits per sample.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_DIGITAL_AUDIO_BITS_PER_SAMPLE (0x01db)

SUMMARY
	Digital Audio Interface bits per sample

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(24)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey defines how many bits the Digital Audio Interface clocks
	per sample. For I2S, if the number of bits per sample is larger than
	the internal audio format used by BlueCore, the additional bits are
	output as zeros in the LSBs.
	
	This PS Key value is used to calculate the port clock rate and so is
	ignored if PSKEY_DIGITAL_AUDIO_RATE is used to define a specific
	rate.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_BCSP_PULL_CONTROL (0x01df)

SUMMARY
	Bus-keeper/pull-disable for BCSP/H5 host transports

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	0x0000

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey configures the enhanced pull device control features
	present on some BlueCore chips for input lines associated with the
	BCSP and H5 host transports (i.e., the UART lines).
	
	The bits in this PSKey only come into effect if BCSP or H5 is selected
	as the host transport at boot time. The selected modes are enabled at
	boot time during BCSP/H5 initialisation and never disabled.
	
	Bit 0 controls "bus-keeper" mode. When an input is in "bus-keeper"
	mode, the polarity of the internal pull device follows that of the
	last externally driven input. (This mode has no effect on pins that
	are driven as outputs by the BlueCore.)
	If this bit is clear (the default), "bus-keeper" mode is never
	enabled; if set, "bus-keeper" mode is enabled at the appropriate time
	by the firmware.
	
	Bit 1 controls "pull-disable" mode. Normally, all inputs have a pull
	device with defined polarity (pull-up or pull-down); in
	"pull-disable" mode, the pull device is disabled entirely, leaving a
	true tri-state input.
	If this bit is clear (the default), the pull device is never
	disabled; if set, the pull device is disabled at the appropriate time
	by the firmware.
	
	Note: In general, if "pull-disable" mode is enabled, the
	"bus-keeper" bit has no effect.
	
	Note: Incorrect configuration of this key can lead to excessive power
	consumption and can potentially damage the chip. If a pull device is
	disabled, but the input is not driven externally (which includes not
	being physically connected, or even not being brought out on the chip
	package), that input floats, leading to excessive current flow.
	
	The default value of this PSKey is safe in this regard.
	"Bus-keeper" mode has no such concerns.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_H4DS_PULL_CONTROL (0x01e0)

SUMMARY
	Bus-keeper/pull-disable for H4DS host transport

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	0x0000

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey configures the enhanced pull device control features
	present on some BlueCore chips for input lines associated with the
	H4DS host transport (i.e., the UART lines). See
	PSKEY_BCSP_PULL_CONTROL for more information on the pull device
	control features.
	
	The bits in this PSKey only come into effect if H4DS is selected as
	the host transport at boot time. The selected modes are enabled at
	boot time during H4DS initialisation and never disabled.
	
	Bit 0 controls "bus-keeper" mode: if this bit is clear (the default),
	"bus-keeper" mode is never enabled; if set, "bus-keeper" mode is
	enabled at the appropriate time by the firmware.
	
	Bit 1 controls "pull-disable" mode: if this bit is clear (the
	default), the pull device is never disabled; if set, the pull device
	is disabled at the appropriate time by the firmware.
	
	Note: Incorrect configuration of this PSKey can lead to excessive
	power consumption and can potentially damage the chip. The default
	value is safe in this regard.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_PCM_PULL_CONTROL (0x01e2)

SUMMARY
	Bus-keeper/pull-disable for PCM bus(es)

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	0x0011

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey configures the enhanced pull device control features
	present on some BlueCore chips for input lines associated with the
	PCM/I2S interface(s). See PSKEY_BCSP_PULL_CONTROL for more information
	on the pull device control features.
	
	The affected lines on each interface are PCM_IN, PCM_OUT, PCM_CLK,
	and PCM_SYNC. Because these can only be controlled as a group, any
	unused lines must be connected and driven appropriately if the pull
	control features are to be used.
	
	There are two complementary bits used to control each feature for
	each PCM interface. One controls the configuration while the
	interface is actively being used to transfer data, and another
	controls the configuration while it is inactive.
	
	The following bits in this PSKey take effect when a PCM interface is
	actively being used by the BlueCore to transfer data:
	
	Bit 0 controls "bus-keeper" mode on the first PCM bus: if this bit is
	clear, "bus-keeper" mode is not enabled during transfers; if set (the
	default), "bus-keeper" mode is enabled during transfers.
	
	Bit 1 controls "pull-disable" mode on the first PCM bus: if this bit
	is clear (the default), the pull device is not disabled during
	transfers; if set, the pull device is disabled during transfers.
	
	The following bits in this key take effect when a PCM interface is
	inactive, and not being used by the BlueCore to transfer data:
	
	Bit 2 controls "bus-keeper" mode on the first PCM bus: if this bit is
	clear (the default), "bus-keeper" mode is not enabled whilst the
	interface is inactive; if set, "bus-keeper" mode is enabled whilst
	the interface is inactive.
	
	Bit 3 controls "pull-disable" mode on the first PCM bus: if this bit
	is clear (the default), the pull device is not disabled whilst the
	interface is inactive; if set, the pull device is disabled whilst the
	interface is inactive.
	
	Bits [7:4] similarly control the second PCM bus, where present.
	
	For Unified-25 firmware and later, the following bits in this key take
	effect when a PCM interface is in the intermediate state:
	
	Bit 8 controls "bus-keeper-disable" mode on the first PCM bus: if this
	bit is clear (the default), "bus-keeper" mode is enabled when the bus
	is in the intermediate state; if set, "bus-keeper" mode is disabled
	when the bus is in the intermediate state.
	
	Bit 9 controls "pull-disable" mode on the first PCM bus: if this bit
	is clear (the default), the pull device is not disabled when the bus
	is in the intermediate state; if set, the pull device is disabled when
	the bus is in the intermediate state.
	
	Bits [13:12] similarly control the second PCM bus, where present.
	
	NOTE: Incorrect configuration of this key can lead to excessive power
	consumption and can potentially damage the chip. The default value is
	safe in this regard.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_MIC_BIAS_PIN_VOLTAGE (0x01e8)

SUMMARY
	Voltage level of hardware Mic Bias pin

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(15)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the voltage level of the hardware MIC_BIAS pin. This 
	pin is only available on some BlueCore variants. The actual voltage 
	level may change between BlueCore variants. See the relevant data
	sheet for more details.
	
	Example values for BlueCore5-MM:
	
	      PSKey  Voltage Range
	        0     1.61 - 1.80 v
	        1     1.65 - 1.86 v
	        2     1.71 - 2.00 v
	        3     1.76 - 1.98 v
	        4     1.84 - 2.06 v
	        5     1.89 - 2.14 v
	        6     1.97 - 2.23 v
	        7     2.04 - 2.32 v
	        8     2.18 - 2.46 v
	        9     2.27 - 2.58 v
	        10    2.39 - 2.72 v
	        11    2.50 - 2.87 v
	        12    2.70 - 3.09 v
	        13    2.85 - 3.29 v
	        14    3.07 - 3.56 v
	        15    3.28 - 3.84 v
	
	Example values for BlueCore7-MM:
	
	      PSKey  Voltage Range
	        0     1.8 v
	        1     2.6 v
	
	Note: This feature only applies to the MIC_BIAS pin and not
	to normal PIO pins.

NAME
	PSKEY_UART_BITRATE (0x01ea)

SUMMARY
	UART baud rate in bits per second

TYPE
	uint32

DEFAULT VALUE
	(38400)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey replaces PSKEY_UART_BAUDRATE for BlueCore7+ chips. 
	
	Setting this PSKey to zero has a special meaning: this triggers the 
	chip to automatically detect the baud rate. This is intended for ROM
	parts.
	
	If this key is non-zero at boot, then the UART is configured to 
	the rate specified by this PSKey in bits per second.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_USB_HOST_WAKE_ENABLE (0x01eb)

SUMMARY
	Enable USB host wakeup

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x0004)        /* both functions disabled */

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey enables the host wakeup mechanism for USB. 
	If the USB host wakeup mechanism is turned on, the firmware judges
	when the peer may have entered its deep sleep state based on timers,
	and the local device can be set to emit a wakeup signal before sending
	data to the peer. Normally, the length of the host wake signal is set 
	to be sufficient to allow the peer to come fully awake because the 
	local device normally sends a message to the peer straight afterwards.
	
	This PSKey also enables another setting, Tx_Remains_Asleep.
	If this setting is enabled the chip assumes that the host remains
	asleep even when it has transmitted data. This means the chip 
	attempts to wake the host whenever it has data to transmit, regardless
	of whether the host transmitted recently or not. The only time it does
	not wake the host for a transmit is if it is transmitting for a second
	time within the host wake period, and so woke the host recently.
	
	This PSKey's value is a bitfield:
	        Bits [3:0]: Enable:       1: enable mechanism
	                                  4: disable mechanism
	        Bit 4: Tx_Remains_Asleep: 1: enabled
	                                  0: disabled
	
	BlueCore use of wakeup signals is disabled by default
	because this suits most systems.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_USB_HOST_WAKE_TIME (0x01ec)

SUMMARY
	USB host wakeup times

TYPE
	uint32[]

DEFAULT VALUE
	{500000, /* microseconds before host sleeps */ 
                        500,     /* microseconds wakeup pulse */ 
                        0}       /* microseconds pause before comms */

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey configures BlueCore use of a wakeup signal to wake the peer
	USB device from a low power state. This wakeup mechanism is enabled 
	via PSKEY_USB_HOST_WAKE_ENABLE. The wakeup signal, which is a pulse 
	on a PIO line, is specified via a separate PSKey, 
	PSKEY_USB_HOST_WAKE_SIGNAL.
	
	This PS key has three uint32 parameters:
	   Sleep_Delay:         Microseconds after tx to host, or rx from 
	                        host after which the host is assumed  
	                        to have gone into its deep sleep state. 
	                        (Range 1 -> 4294967295)
	   HWake_Signal_Length: Minimum duration of wake signal in 
	                        microseconds.
	                        (Range 0 -> 1000000)
	   Pause_Length:        Microseconds between end of wake signal 
	                        and sending of data to the host. 
	                        (Range 0 -> 1000000) 
	
	The minimum HWake_Signal_Length that can actually be produced is 
	15us achieved by setting the value to 0us. 

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_USB_HOST_WAKE_SIGNAL (0x01ed)

SUMMARY
	Signal to use for the USB host wakeup protocol

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	0x0031

DESCRIPTION
	If the host wakeup mechanism for USB is enabled via 
	PSKEY_USB_HOST_WAKE_ENABLE, this PSKey can specify the
	wakeup signal to use: either a positive or negative pulse on a PIO
	line.
	
	This PSKey's value is a bitfield:
	        Bits [3:0]: Host Wake Mechanism. 1 => positive pulse on PIO
	                                         2 => negative pulse on PIO
	        Bits [7:4]: PIO pin selection.   Value selects PIO pin.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_USB_DATA_PLUS_PULL_CONTROL (0x01f0)

SUMMARY
	Signal to determine when D+ is activated on boot

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(AS_SOON_AS_POSSIBLE)

ENUM_INCLUDE_FILE
	io_bt.h

ENUM_VALUES
	AS_SOON_AS_POSSIBLE   sets D+ at boot (<100ms)
	AFTER_CONFIGURATION   sets D+ when configuration is done (when ready)

DESCRIPTION
	By default, D+ pullup is activated during initialization as per the
	USB standard. If PSKEY_USB_DATA_PLUS_PULL_CONTROL is set to
	AFTER_CONFIGURATION ('sets D+ when configuration is done'), D+ pullup
	is only activated when configuration is complete.
	If PSKEY_USB_CHARGER_DETECTION_ENABLE is set to 'Voltage source
	detection' then the value of PSKEY_USB_DATA_PLUS_PULL_CONTROL is
	ignored and the firmware always acts as if 
	PSKEY_USB_DATA_PLUS_PULL_CONTROL has been set to AFTER_CONFIGURATION
	('sets D+ when configuration is done').

NAME
	PSKEY_AUDIO_DECOUPLE_CAP (0x01f4)

SUMMARY
	audio decouple capacitor

TYPE
	uint8

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(0x3)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0x3)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey specifies an override to the default audio decoupling
	setting. This PSKey is read at audio initialisation and set if
	present.
	
	For HAVE_GORDON_AUDIO these values are assigned from the enumeration:
	0: decoupling off (bad audio)
	1: 0.5V reference (best for DAC)
	2: 0.7V reference (best for ADC)
	3: 0.95V reference (best for mic bias)
	

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_WD_TIMEOUT (0x01f7)

SUMMARY
	Watchdog timeout (microseconds)

TYPE
	TIME

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(60 * SECOND)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(5 * SECOND)

DESCRIPTION
	BlueCore has hardware support to run a watchdog timer. This is a
	timer that is set to the value of this PSKey every time it is
	"kicked" (written to by the firmware). If the firmware fails to
	kick the watchdog within this period the chip's watchdog hardware
	forces a hardware reset of the chip. This supports the
	possibility that the chip's firmware might crash or hang
	up.
	
	The value is in microseconds. If the value is zero the watchdog is
	disabled.
	
	This PSKey is used in conjunction with PSKEY_ENABLE_SOFT_WD to enable 
	the watchdog in its debug mode.
	See description of PSKEY_ENABLE_SOFT_WD.
	
	Also see the description of PSKEY_WD_PERIOD.
	
	Type TIME is fundamentally a uint32.  Value SECOND is 1000000.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_WD_PERIOD (0x01f8)

SUMMARY
	Watchdog period (microseconds)

TYPE
	TIME

MINIMUM
	(100 * MILLISECOND)

MAXIMUM
	(60 * SECOND)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(3 * SECOND)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the watchdog period, (nominally) the microseconds
	between kicking the watchdog hardware.
	
	This should be no more than 70% of PSKEY_WD_TIMEOUT (unless the
	timeout value is zero).
	
	Type TIME is fundamentally a uint32.  Value SECOND is 1000000.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HOST_INTERFACE (0x01f9)

SUMMARY
	Host interface

TYPE
	phys_bus

DEFAULT VALUE
	(phys_bus_bcsp)

ENUM_INCLUDE_FILE
	io_bt.h

ENUM_VALUES
	phys_bus_none   No host to chip connection
	phys_bus_bcsp   UART link running BCSP
	 phys_bus_usb   USB link
	  phys_bus_h4   UART link running H4
	 phys_bus_usr   VM access to the UART
	  phys_bus_h5   UART link running H5
	phys_bus_h4ds   UART link running H4 with deep sleep
	phys_bus_sdio   SDIO or CSPI link

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey selects the physical connection that is used to pass 
	information to and from the host - BCSP, H4, USB, etc.  Only one of 
	these can be used at a time, mainly because the USB interface uses 
	some of the same chip pins as the UART.
	
	Much of the chip's support for BCSP/H5 is performed by hardware. This 
	allows interrupt routines to deal with complete BCSP/H5 packets.
	When the chip uses its UART in a more naive fashion, e.g., for H4,
	this support must be disabled. The UART's hardware support for
	BCSP/H5 must be enabled via PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_BCSP/H5.
	
	The H4 specification requires the use of UART hardware flow control
	and no use of parity. These must also be set via PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_H4.
	
	Type phys_bus is really a uint16. The PSKey takes values:
	
	        0: No chip to host connection
	        1: BCSP
	        2: H2 - USB
	        3: H4 - UART
	        4: VM access to the UART
	        6: H5
	        7: H4DS
	        9: SDIO
	
	Note: The "H5" host transport protocol is properly known as the 
	"Three-Wire  UART Transport Layer", but is commonly known as H5 
	within CSR.
	

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HQ_HOST_TIMEOUT (0x01fb)

SUMMARY
	HQ host command timeout

TYPE
	TIME

MINIMUM
	(1 * SECOND)

MAXIMUM
	(60 * SECOND)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(5 * SECOND)

DESCRIPTION
	Each HQ (host query) message sent to the host should provoke a 
	corresponding reply from the host. This PSKey sets the period in 
	microseconds for which the HQ  task waits before giving up 
	waiting for the reply.
	
	Type TIME is fundamentally a uint32.  Value SECOND is 1000000.
	
	See PSKEY_HQ_ACTIVE.
	
	For more information see the CSR documents "HQ Protocol", CS-102660-SP
	and "BlueCore HQ Commands", CS-101607-SP.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_HQ_ACTIVE (0x01fc)

SUMMARY
	Enable Host Query Task

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(TRUE)

DESCRIPTION
	The device's HQ (host query) task can send messages to the host over
	either BCSP channel 3 or tunnelled through the CSR 
	manufacturer-specific HCI extensions. The channel's protocol has an 
	RPC-style structure. This means each message should cause the host to 
	send a corresponding response back to the chip. The protocol is 
	described in document "HQ Protocol", CS-102660-SP, available from the 
	CSR support website.
	
	If PSKEY_HQ_ACTIVE is set to TRUE (1), then the device's HQ task is
	enabled. If PSKEY_HQ_ACTIVE is set to FALSE (0), then the device's
	HQ task is configured so that no HQ traffic is sent to the host.
	
	See PSKEY_HQ_HOST_TIMEOUT.
	
	For more information see the CSR documents "HQ Protocol", CS-102660-SP
	and "BlueCore HQ Commands", CS-101607-SP.
	
	Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to
	FALSE and TRUE.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_BCCMD_SECURITY_ACTIVE (0x01fd)

SUMMARY
	Enable configuration security

TYPE
	bool

DEFAULT VALUE
	(FALSE)

DESCRIPTION
	The firmware's bccmd task presents a command interpreter to the host
	in a manner similar to HCI. The command interpreter's command set is
	not part of any Bluetooth standard. It is specific to the BlueCore
	chips and firmware. The command set is used for monitoring and 
	controlling the chip, running radio tests, etc. The command set is 
	described in document "BCCMD Commands," CS-101482-SP.
	
	The command interpreter is accessed via the BCCMD protocol. The BCCMD
	protocol is described in document "BCCMD Protocol",
	CS-101676-SP. This can run over a BCSP channel (channel 2, see 
	document "BCSP Channel Allocation", CS-101680-SP), over a CSR 
	manufacturer-specific HCI extension channel or over the chip's SPI 
	interface.
	
	The bccmd task provides a simple access control mechanism for BCCMD
	commands presented over BCSP or HCI-extension; this mechanism is not
	present for SPI access.
	
	This PSKey enables the security mechanism. The security mechanism is
	described in the document "BCCMD Protocol Security", CS-101679-SP.
	
	When a BlueCore module is freshly manufactured this bool flag is set
	FALSE. The host may then read and write all PS values and can run
	all of the BCCMD commands. This allows the manufacturer to configure
	the Bluetooth module.
	
	When the configuration is complete the manufacturer sets this PSKey
	to TRUE. This enables the PS and BCCMD access controls. When set
	TRUE this PSKey cannot be set back to FALSE via BCSP running over the
	BCSP extension channel or the HCI extension channel. Setting security
	active is therefore normally a one-way operation.
	
	Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to
	FALSE and TRUE.
	
	For more information see "BCCMD Protocol Security", CS-101679-SP, 
	"BCCMD Protocol", CS-101676-SP, "BCCMD Commands," CS-101482-SP and 
	"BCSP Channel Allocation", CS-101680-SP.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_ANA_FREQ (0x01fe)

SUMMARY
	Crystal frequency

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(26000)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey configures the BlueCore hardware to work with a particular 
	reference clock frequency.
	
	For chips prior to BlueCore2-ROM the default, 4, configures the chip
	to use a 16 MHz reference. The value defines a reference frequency
	of n*250 kHz where n is an integer, but there is a pseudo-random
	mapping from n to the required value. This is described in supporting
	documentation. 
	
	For BlueCore2-ROM and subsequent chips, the value defines the
	reference frequency in units of 1 kHz. The default value, 26000,
	configures the chip to use a 26 MHz reference. If the PSKey is absent
	or the value is zero, the chip attempts to pick a frequency;
	this cannot be relied on to be the correct frequency, so the radio
	is not usable.
	
	The automatic clock frequency detection mechanism is likely to be most
	useful in ROM parts, and is described in document "Booting BlueCore 
	ROM", CS-101436-ME, available from the CSR support website.
	
	When an external crystal is in use, it is usually necessary to make
	fine adjustments to allow for variations in individual crystals.
	See the description of PSKEY_ANA_FTRIM and PSKEY_ANA_FTRIM_OFFSET for
	details.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_PIO_PROTECT_MASK (0x0202)

SUMMARY
	Access to PIO0 - PIO15 pins

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0)

DESCRIPTION
	Each BlueCore chip contains a PIO port that may, under BCCMD or VM
	control, be used as a general I/O port. However, various
	optional hardware and software configurations require the use of
	certain PIO pins for their own needs. For example, an optional 
	external PA/LNA block may be driven using PIO pins 0 and 1.
	
	This PSKey prevents applications from changing PIO pins that are
	required for lower level functions. This blocking action applies
	to host-based applications requesting PIO changes via BCCMD and
	to VM applications running on the chip.
	
	Some of the lower level functions automatically prevent the
	application from changing the state of PIOs being used by the
	function by overriding the value of the relevant bits in this
	PSKey. This includes the PIOs related to PSKEY_TXRX_PIO_CONTROL,
	PSKEY_USB_PIO_VBUS, PSKEY_USB_PIO_DETACH, PSKEY_USB_PIO_PULLUP,
	PSKEY_USB_PIO_WAKEUP and PSKEY_USB_PIO_RESUME. So, for example
	if PSKEY_USB_PIO_DETACH claims the use of PIO[5] then this PIO
	cannot be changed by application code no matter what the value
	of PSKEY_PIO_PROTECT_MASK is.
	
	Bits [7:0] of this uint16 PSKey map to PIO0 to PIO7 respectively.
	If a bit of the PSKey's value is set high then application code
	cannot change the value of the corresponding PIO port pin.
	
	Note: On the current Casira motherboard, PIO2 is connected to USB+
	via a 1k5 resistor. The USB+ pin doubles as the UART RTS line on
	BlueCore, so care must be taken if an application uses PIO2.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_STUB (0x0207)

SUMMARY
	Stub

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0)

DESCRIPTION
	A key that can be harmlessly read or written.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_TXRX_PIO_CONTROL (0x0209)

SUMMARY
	TX and RX PIO control

TYPE
	uint16

DEFAULT VALUE
	(0)

ENUM_VALUES
	0   PIO does not drive tx+rx, internal amp ramps power
	1   PIO drives tx+rx, internal amp ramps power
	2   PIO drives tx+rx, aux dac ramps external amp gain
	3   PIO drives tx+rx inverted, internal amp ramps power
	4   PIO drives tx+rx, internal amp ramps power, aux dac sets external amp gain
	5   PIO drives tx+rx, internal amp ramps power, aux dac sets external LNA

DESCRIPTION
	The chip contains a radio power amplifier (PA) and low noise
	amplifier (LNA), allowing it to act as a limited-range Bluetooth
	device. Although this is adequate for many applications, some
	systems require more range and so use external PA/LNA devices.
	
	If external devices are used, two pins of the PIO port are allocated
	to control them. On BlueCore7 onwards, the pins used are configurable
	by PSKEY_TXRX_PIO_TX and PSKEY_TXRX_PIO_RX. On earlier chips the LNA
	is enabled by pin PIO0 and the PA by pin PIO1.
	
	Before transmitting, the chip normally ramps up the power to the
	internal PA, then it ramps it down again afterwards.  However, if a
	suitable external PA is used it may be possible to ramp the power
	externally using the AUX_DAC pin.
	
	This PSKey sets the PA/LNA configuration:
	
	    0: The two PIO lines are not driven for Tx and Rx.  The chip's
	        internal PA/LNA is used.
	
	    1: The two PIO lines are driven high to enable the external PA
	        and LNA. Tx power ramping is controlled by the internal PA.
	
	    2: The two PIO lines are driven high to enable the external PA
	        and LNA. Tx power ramping is controlled on the external PA
	        via the chip's AUX_DAC pin.  The
	        "external_pa" entries in PSKEY_POWER_TABLE are used.
	
	    3: The two PIO lines are driven low to enable the external PA
	        and LNA. Tx power ramping is controlled by the internal PA.
	
	    4: PIO lines driven high for external PA and LNA;
	        Tx power ramping controlled by internal PA. External PA 
	        controlled (not ramped) by chip's AUX_DAC pin. The 
	        "external_pa" entries in PSKEY_POWER_TABLE are used.
	
	    5: PIO lines driven high for external PA and LNA;
	        Tx power ramping controlled by internal PA.  External LNA
	        gain controlled by chip's AUX_DAC pin. The AUX_DAC
	        is varied by the AGC between zero and its maximum in 16 steps.
	
	Hardware restrictions prevent the use of active low PIO pins and
	external PA ramping.
	
	The behaviour of the chip's AUX_DAC pin is undefined unless this key
	is set to 2 or 4.
	
	See also:
	        PSKEY_LC_MAX_TX_POWER
	        PSKEY_TX_GAIN_RAMP
	        PSKEY_LC_POWER_TABLE
	        PSKEY_LC_DEFAULT_TX_POWER
	        PSKEY_TXRX_PIO_TX
	        PSKEY_TXRX_PIO_RX.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_ANA_RX_LEVEL (0x020b)

SUMMARY
	ANA_RX_LVL register initial value

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(16)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(3)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the initial value of the chip's $ANA_RX_LVL register.
	
	Do not alter the value of this PSKey except with specific advice from 
	CSR.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_PCM0_ATTENUATION (0x020f)

SUMMARY
	Volume control on PCM channels

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(7)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(3)

DESCRIPTION
	Some Motorola codecs allow their gain to be controlled by 3 extra
	bits received at the end of a 13 bit PCM sample.
	
	This PSKey sets the value of these three bits for SCO data sent from
	chip's PCM channels (channels 0-3 on PCM1 and PCM2, if exists). It 
	is expected that low values will map to high volume levels, though
	the firmware has no knowledge of this: it just passes the bits into
	the PCM stream. If this value is not needed then it may make sense
	to set this key to zero.
	
	It is possible that the firmware will acquire dynamically-settable
	attenuation controls for the PCM channel(s). In this case this
	PSKey will set the initial attenuation value.

==============================================================================
NAME
	PSKEY_IQ_TRIM_CHANNEL (0x0214)

SUMMARY
	IQ calibration channel

TYPE
	uint16

MINIMUM
	(0)

MAXIMUM
	(78)

DEFAULT VALUE
	(44)

DESCRIPTION
	This PSKey sets the Bluetooth radio channel on which to perform IQ 
	trim auto calibration. For most of the world this can be in the range 
	0..78. For France it must be in the range 54..76.  If the value in
	this PSKey is out of range for France and the firmware detects that it
	is in France (by using the country code) then the value is
	silently brought into range.

NAME
	PSKEY_TX_OFFSET_HALF_MHZ (0x0217)

SUMMARY
	Transmit offset

TYPE
	int16

MINIMUM
	(-16)

MAXIMUM
	(15)

	For BlueCore5+ it controls only the basic rate Class 2 transmit
	offset.
	
	Do not alter the value of this PSKey except with specific advice from
